Section 1:
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
2 INTRODUCED BY C. GLIMM
3
4 A BILL FOR AN ACT ENTITLED: “AN ACT FOR THE CODIFICATION AND GENERAL REVISION OF THE
5 LAWS RELATING TO THE DEFINITION FOR THE WORDS SEX, FEMALE, AND MALE, MAN, WOMAN,
6 FATHER, AND MOTHER WHEN REFERRING TO A HUMAN; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX
7 REFERS TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT GENDER IDENTITY OR SEXUAL INTERCOURSE; PROVIDING
8 THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX IS LIMITED TO TWO TYPES OF SEXES WHICH ARE REFERRED TO AS
9 MALE AND FEMALE; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITIONS OF MALE, AND FEMALE, MAN, WOMAN,
10 FATHER, AND MOTHER REFER TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT SUBJECTIVE GENDER IDENTITY;
11 CLARIFYING THE MEANING OF THE TERM "GENDER"; AMENDING SECTIONS 2-18-208, 2-18-606, 7-15-
12 4207, 7-34-2123, 10-2-403, 13-27-408, 13-35-301, 13-38-201, 13-38-203, 13-38-205, 19-2-802, 20-6-808, 20-
13 7-1306, 20-7-1703, 20-9-327, 20-11-116, 20-25-501, 20-25-707, 22-2-306, 23-2-505, 33-1-201, 35-20-209, 39-
14 2-912, 39-29-101, 39-71-401, 40-1-107, 40-1-311, 40-1-401, 40-5-804, 40-5-907, 40-5-1031, 40-6-701, 40-6-
15 703, 41-3-210, 41-5-103, 42-2-204, 44-2-411, 44-2-412, 45-5-625, 46-18-101, 46-19-301, 46-19-401, 49-1-102,
16 49-2-101, 49-3-101, 50-4-720, 50-5-105, 50-5-602, 50-11-101, 50-15-101, 50-19-103, 50-19-501, 50-60-214,
17 53-20-142, 53-21-121, 53-21-142, 53-24-310, 53-30-312, 60-5-514, 60-5-522, 61-5-107, 72-1-103, 72-17-106,
18 AND 90-14-104, MCA; REPEALING SECTION 1-1-201, MCA; AND PROVIDING AN IMMEDIATE EFFECTIVE
19 DATE.”
20
21 WHEREAS, in human beings, there are two -- and only two -- sexes: male and female, which refer to
22 the two body structures (phenotypes) that, in normal development, correspond to one or the other gamete --
23 sperm for males and ova for females; and
24 WHEREAS, every individual is either male or female; and
25 WHEREAS, an individual's sex can be observed or clinically verified at or before birth; and
26 WHEREAS, rare disorders of sexual development are not exceptions to the binary nature of sex; and
27
28 WHEREAS, in no case is an individual's sex determined by stipulation or self-identification; and
- 1 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 WHEREAS, there is increasing confusion about the definition and implications of sex as a biological
2 truth and its relationship to concepts and terms including but not limited to sex assigned at birth, gender, gender
3 identity, gender role, gender expression, and experienced gender; and
4 WHEREAS, confusion and ambiguities surrounding the definitions of sex, male, female, and related
5 terms can hinder individual efforts to enjoy equal treatment under the law; and
6 WHEREAS, legal equality of the two sexes -- male and female -- does not imply that the sexes are
7 identical to each other or are the same in every respect; and
8 WHEREAS, with respect to the two sexes -- male and female -- separate facilities or sports leagues
9 established because of or organized according to physical differences between the sexes do not constitute
10 unequal treatment under the law; and
11 WHEREAS, physical differences between males and females are enduring, and the two sexes are not
12 fungible.
13 THEREFORE, it is the intent of the Legislature of this state to clarify and reconcile the meaning of sex,
14 male, female, and related terms in state laws, administrative rules, and guidelines.
15
16 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF THE STATE OF MONTANA:
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 1. Terms of wide applicability. (1) Unless the context requires otherwise,
19 the following definitions apply in the Montana Code Annotated:
20 (a) "FATHER" MEANS A MALE PARENT.
21 (B) "Female" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XX
22 chromosomes and produces or would produce relatively large, relatively immobile gametes, or eggs, during her
23 life cycle and has a reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An
24 individual who would otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is female, WHEN
25 USED TO REFER TO A NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT
26 FOR A CONGENITAL ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT
27 SOME POINT PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE LARGE GAMETE, OR OVA, FOR FERTILIZATION.
28 (b) (C) "Male" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XY
- 2 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 chromosomes and produces or would produce small, mobile gametes, or sperm, during his life cycle and has a
2 reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An individual who would
3 otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is male, WHEN USED TO REFER TO A
4 NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT FOR A CONGENITAL
5 ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT SOME POINT
6 PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE SMALL GAMETE, OR SPERM, FOR FERTILIZATION.
7 (c) (D) "MAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN MALE, EXCEPT WHEN USED AS A GENERIC REFERENCE TO HUMAN
8 BEINGS.
9 (E) "MOTHER" MEANS A FEMALE PARENT.
10 (F) "Oath" includes an affirmation or declaration.
11 (d) (G) "Person" includes a corporation or other entity as well as a natural person.
12 (e) (H) "Several" means two or more.
13 (f) (I) "Sex" means the organization of the body parts and gametes for reproduction in human beings
14 and other organisms. In human beings, there are exactly two sexes, male and female, with two corresponding
15 types of gametes. The sexes are determined by the biological and genetic indication of male or female,
16 including sex chromosomes, naturally occurring sex chromosomes, gonads, and nonambiguous internal and
17 external genitalia present at birth, without regard to an individual's psychological, behavioral, social, chosen, or
18 subjective experience of gender WHETHER SOMEONE IS MALE OR FEMALE, WHICH IS DISTINGUISHED BASED ON THE
19 TYPE OF GAMETE, SPERM OR EGGS, THEY ARE CAPABLE OF OR EXPECTED TO PRODUCE, AS DICTATED BY THEIR PRIMARY
20 SEXUAL ANATOMY. BECAUSE THERE ARE ONLY TWO TYPES OF GAMETES, SPERM AND OVA, WITH TWO CORRESPONDING
21 REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEMS, THERE ARE ONLY TWO SEXES: MALE AND FEMALE. AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX IS ROOTED IN
22 REPRODUCTIVE ANATOMY AND IS IN NO WAY INFLUENCED OR DEFINED BY ONE'S PSYCHOLOGICAL STATE, BEHAVIOR,
23 EXPRESSION, OR PERSONAL IDENTITY.
24 (g) (J) "State", when applied to the different parts of the United States, includes the District of
25 Columbia and the territories.
26 (h) (K) "United States" includes the District of Columbia and the territories.
27 (L) "WOMAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN FEMALE.
28 (2) Wherever the word "man" or "men" or a word that includes the syllable "man" or "men" in
- 3 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 combination with other syllables, such as "workman", appears in this code, the word or syllable includes
2 "woman" or "women" unless the context clearly indicates a contrary intent and unless the subject matter of the
3 statute relates clearly and necessarily to a specific sex only.
4 (3) Whenever the term "heretofore" occurs in any statute, it must be construed to mean any time
5 previous to the day the statute takes effect. Whenever the word "hereafter" occurs, it must be construed to
6 mean the time after the statute containing the term takes effect.
7 (4) (A) THE TERM "GENDER", WHEN USED ALONE TO REFER TO A MALE, FEMALE, OR THE NATURAL
8 DIFFERENCES BETWEEN A MALE AND FEMALE:
9 (I) MUST BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM FOR SEX; AND
10 (II) MAY NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SHORT-HAND EXPRESSION FOR GENDER IDENTITY,
11 EXPERIENCED GENDER, GENDER EXPRESSION, OR GENDER ROLE.
12 (B) THE TERM "GENDER" DOES NOT APPLY WHEN IT IS USED IN CONJUNCTION WITH OTHER WORDS OR AS
13 AN ADJECTIVE TO MODIFY OTHER WORDS, OR WHEN CONTEXT OR EXPLICIT DEFINITION IN PREEXISTING STATE LAW,
14 ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES INDICATES OTHERWISE.
15 (C) THE TERM "GENDER IDENTITY", IF USED IN STATE LAW, ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES, MAY
16 NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SUBSTITUTE FOR SEX OR GENDER.
17
18 Section 2. Section 2-18-208, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "2-18-208. Comparable worth. The department of administration shall, in its continuous efforts to
20 enhance the current classification plan and pay schedules, work toward the goal of establishing a standard of
21 equal pay for comparable worth. This standard for the classification plan shall be reached by:
22 (1) eliminating, in the classification of positions, the use of judgments and factors that contain
23 inherent biases based on sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1]; and
24 (2) comparing, in the classification of positions, the factors for determining job worth across
25 occupational groups whenever those groups are dominated by males or females."
26
27 SECTION 3. Section 2-18-606, MCA, is amended to read:
28 "2-18-606. Parental leave for state employees. (1) The department of administration shall develop a
- 4 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 parental leave policy for permanent state employees. The policy must permit an employee to take a reasonable
2 leave of absence and permit the employee to use sick leave immediately following the birth or placement of a
3 child for a period not to exceed 15 working days if:
4 (a) the employee is adopting a child; or
5 (b) the employee is a birth father, as defined in [section 1].
6 (2) As used in this section, "placement" means placement for adoption as defined in 33-22-130.
7 (3) A state agency that is not subject to the provisions of the Family and Medical Leave Act of
8 1993, 29 U.S.C. 2601 through 2654, may extend the provisions of that act to the employees of the agency."

10 Section 4. Section 7-15-4207, MCA, is amended to read:
11 "7-15-4207. Prohibition against discrimination. For all of the purposes of this part and part 43, a
12 person may not be subjected to discrimination because of sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], race, creed,
13 religion, age, physical or mental disability, color, or national origin."
14
15 Section 5. Section 7-34-2123, MCA, is amended to read:
16 "7-34-2123. Admission to district hospital facilities. Such a hospital district must admit persons to
17 its facilities without regard to race, color, or sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1]. Such obligation shall not
18 prevent the board of trustees of such hospital district from establishing reasonable minimum rates for hospital
19 quarters, services, and supplies. Indigents needing such services, for the rendition of which provision is made
20 by the laws of Montana, must be admitted to such public hospitals on terms and rates prescribed or authorized
21 by law."

23 SECTION 6. Section 10-2-403, MCA, is amended to read:
24 "10-2-403. Eligibility for residence in home. To be eligible for residence in a Montana veterans'
25 home under rules prescribed by the department of public health and human services, a person must be a
26 veteran or the spouse or surviving spouse of a veteran. Consideration must also be given to:
27 (1) the person's age;
28 (2) the person's physical and mental status;
- 5 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (3) the person's ability or inability to locate suitable alternative accommodations;
2 (4) the person's term of residence in Montana;
3 (5) the person's gender, as provided in [section 1], as it relates to availability of appropriate living
4 space;
5 (6) the ability of the Montana veterans' home to meet the person's needs; and
6 (7) other admission requirements established by the department."

8 Section 7. Section 13-27-408, MCA, is amended to read:
9 "13-27-408. Rejection of improper arguments. The secretary of state shall reject, with the approval
10 of the attorney general, an argument or other matter held to contain obscene, vulgar, profane, scandalous,
11 libelous, or defamatory matter; any language that in any way incites, counsels, promotes, or advocates hatred,
12 abuse, violence, or hostility toward, or that tends to cast ridicule or shame upon, a group of persons by reason
13 of race, color, religion, or sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1]; or any matter not allowed to be sent through
14 the mail. Such arguments may not be filed or printed in the voter information pamphlet."
15
16 Section 8. Section 13-35-301, MCA, is amended to read:
17 "13-35-301. Adoption of code of fair campaign practices. The following code of fair campaign
18 practices is adopted by Montana:
19 "There are basic principles of decency, honesty, and fair play that every candidate for public office in
20 the United States has a moral obligation to observe and uphold, in order that, after vigorously contested but
21 fairly conducted campaigns, our citizens may exercise their constitutional right to a free and untrammeled
22 choice and the will of the people may be fully and clearly expressed on the issues before the country.
23 Therefore:
24 I will conduct my campaign in the best American tradition, discussing the issues as I see them,
25 presenting my record and policies with sincerity and frankness, and criticizing without fear or favor the record
26 and policies of my opponent and my opponent's party that merit such criticism.
27 I will defend and uphold the right of every qualified American voter to full and equal participation in the
28 electoral process.
- 6 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 I will conduct my campaign without the use of personal vilification, character defamation, whispering
2 campaigns, libel, slander, or scurrilous attacks on my opposition or my opposition's personal or family life.
3 I will not use campaign material of any sort that misrepresents, distorts, or otherwise falsifies the facts,
4 nor will I use malicious or unfounded accusations that aim at creating or exploiting doubts, without justification,
5 as to the loyalty and patriotism of my opposition.
6 I will not make any appeal to prejudice based on race, sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], creed, or
7 national origin.
8 I will not undertake or condone any dishonest or unethical practice that tends to corrupt or undermine
9 our American system of free elections or that hampers or prevents the full and free expression of the will of the
10 voters.
11 Insofar as is possible, I will immediately and publicly repudiate support deriving from any individual or
12 group that resorts, on behalf of my candidacy or in opposition to that of my opponent, to the methods and
13 tactics that I have pledged not to use or condone.""
14
15 Section 9. Section 13-38-201, MCA, is amended to read:
16 "13-38-201. Election or appointment of committee representatives at primary -- vacancies -- tie
17 votes. (1) Each political party shall appoint or elect at each primary election one person of each sex, as defined
18 in 1-1-201 [section 1], to serve as committee representatives for each election precinct. The committee
19 representatives must be residents and registered voters of the precinct.
20 (2) If a political party chooses to appoint precinct committee representatives, the political party
21 shall make the appointments as provided in the party's rules.
22 (3) If a political party chooses to elect precinct committee representatives, the party may:
23 (a) administer the election itself as provided in the party's rules; or
24 (b) elect precinct committee representatives in a primary election, subject to 13-10-209 and
25 subsection (4) of this section.
26 (4) In a primary election for a precinct committee representative:
27 (a) if the number of candidates nominated for a party's precinct committee representatives is less
28 than or equal to the number of positions to be elected, the election administrator may give notice that a party's
- 7 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 precinct committee election will not be held in that precinct;
2 (b) if a party precinct committee election is not held pursuant to subsection (4)(a), the election
3 administrator shall declare elected by acclamation the candidate who filed for the position or who filed a
4 declaration of intent to be a write-in candidate. The election administrator shall issue a certificate of election to
5 the designated party.
6 (c) write-in votes for a precinct committee representative may be counted as specified in 13-15-
7 206(5) only if the individual whose name is written in has filed a declaration of intent as a write-in candidate by
8 the deadline prescribed in 13-10-211(1);
9 (d) in the case of a tie vote for a precinct committee representative position, the county central
10 committee shall determine a winner.
11 (5) Pursuant to 13-38-101, a vacancy in a precinct committee representative position must be filled
12 by the party governing body as provided in its rules."
13
14 SECTION 10. Section 13-38-203, MCA, is amended to read:
15 "13-38-203. Powers and duties of county and city central committees -- role of state central
16 committee where no county central committee exists. (1) The county and city central committee may:
17 (a) make rules for the government of its political party in each county not inconsistent with any of
18 the provisions of the election laws of this state or the rules of its state political party;
19 (b) elect two county members of the state central committee, one of each gender, as provided in
20 [section 1], elect the members of the congressional committee, and fill all vacancies and make rules in their
21 jurisdiction.
22 (2) If there is no county central committee, the state central committee shall appoint a county
23 central committee.
24 (3) Meetings of a central committee that is filling an election vacancy pursuant to 13-10-326 or 13-
25 10-327 must be open to the public. Records of a central committee regarding filling a vacancy pursuant to 13-
26 10-326 or 13-10-327 must be made available for public inspection on request.
27 (4) County and city central committees are not public agencies of the state. The documents of the
28 county and city central committees are not public records."

2 SECTION 11. Section 13-38-205, MCA, is amended to read:
3 "13-38-205. Organization and operation of county and city central committees. (1) The county
4 central committee shall meet prior to the state convention of its political party and organize by electing a
5 presiding officer and one or more vice presiding officers. The gender, as provided in [section 1], of the presiding
6 officer and the vice presiding officer may not be the same. The county central committee shall elect a secretary
7 and other officers as necessary. It is not necessary for the officers to be precinct committee representatives.
8 (2) The committee may select managing or executive committees and authorize subcommittees to
9 exercise all powers conferred upon the county, city, state, and congressional central committees by the election
10 laws of this state.
11 (3) The presiding officer of the county central committee shall call the county convention and not
12 less than 4 days before the date of the county convention shall publish the call in a newspaper published at the
13 county seat and mail a copy of the call to each precinct committee representative. If party rules permit the use
14 of a proxy, a proxy may not be recognized unless it is held by an elector of the precinct of the committee
15 representative executing it.
16 (4) The county presiding officer of the party shall preside at the county convention. No person
17 other than a duly elected or appointed committee representative or officer of the committee is entitled to
18 participate in the proceedings of the committee.
19 (5) If a committee representative is absent, the convention may fill the vacancy by appointing some
20 qualified elector of the party, resident in the precinct, to represent the precinct in the convention.
21 (6) The county convention shall elect delegates and alternate delegates to the state convention
22 under rules of the state party. The presiding officer and secretary of the county convention shall issue and sign
23 certificates of election of the delegates."
24
25 SECTION 12. Section 19-2-802, MCA, is amended to read:
26 "19-2-802. Effect of no designation of beneficiary or no surviving statutory or designated
27 beneficiary. (1) If a member or payment recipient fails to name a designated beneficiary or if a statutory or
28 designated beneficiary does not survive the member or payment recipient, the estate of the member or
- 9 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 payment recipient is entitled to any accrued lump-sum payment or accrued retirement benefit not received prior
2 to the member's or payment recipient's death. If the estate, as either a designated beneficiary or as a
3 beneficiary by default as provided in this subsection, would not be probated but for the amount due to the
4 estate from the retirement system, all of the amount due to the estate must be paid directly, without probate, to
5 the surviving next of kin of the deceased or the guardians of the survivor's estate, share and share alike.
6 (2) Payment must be made in the same order in which the following groups are listed:
7 (a) husband or wife;
8 (b) children;
9 (c) father and mother, as defined in [section 1];
10 (d) grandchildren;
11 (e) brothers and sisters; or
12 (f) nieces and nephews.
13 (3) A payment may not be made to a person included in any of the groups listed in subsection (2) if
14 at the date of payment there is a living person in any of the groups preceding the group of which the person is a
15 member, as listed. Payment must be made upon receipt from the person of an affidavit, upon a form supplied
16 by the board, that there are no living individuals in the groups preceding the group of which the person is a
17 member and that the estate of the deceased will not be probated.
18 (4) The payment must be in full and complete discharge and acquittance of the board and system
19 on account of the member's or payment recipient's death."

21 SECTION 13. Section 20-6-808, MCA, is amended to read:
22 "20-6-808. Enrollment. (1) (a) A public charter school must be open to any student residing in the
23 state.
24 (b) A school district may not require a student enrolled in the school district to attend a public
25 charter school.
26 (c) A public charter school may limit admission to students within a given age group or grade level.
27 (d) A public charter school may be organized for a special emphasis, theme, or concept as stated
28 in the school's proposal.
- 10 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (e) A public charter school shall enroll all students who wish to attend the school unless the
2 number of students exceeds the capacity of a program, class, grade level, or building.
3 (f) If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend the school, the public charter
4 school shall select students through a lottery.
5 (2) (a) A public charter school shall give enrollment preference to students who are residents of the
6 located school district.
7 (b) A public charter school may give enrollment preference to:
8 (i) students who were enrolled in the public charter school the previous school year and to siblings
9 of students already enrolled in the public charter school. An enrollment preference for returning students
10 excludes those students from entering a lottery.
11 (ii) children of members of a public charter school's governing board and full-time employees,
12 limited to no more than 10% of the school's total student population.
13 (3) This section does not preclude the formation of a public charter school for the purpose of
14 serving students with disabilities, students of the same gender, as provided in [section 1], students who pose a
15 sufficiently severe disciplinary problem to warrant a specific educational program, or students who are at risk of
16 academic failure. If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend such a school, the public
17 charter school shall select students through a lottery.
18 (4) If a student who was previously enrolled in a public charter school enrolls in any other public
19 school in this state, the student's new school shall accept credits earned by the student in courses or
20 instructional programs at the public charter school.
21 (5) A school district shall provide or publicize to parents and the general public information about
22 public charter schools as an enrollment option within the district to the same extent and through the same
23 means that the district provides and publicizes information about noncharter public schools in the district.
24 (6) The board of public education may not restrict the number of students a public charter school
25 may enroll. The capacity of the public charter school must be determined annually by the governing board in
26 consideration of the public charter school's ability to facilitate the academic success of its students, to achieve
27 the objectives specified in the charter contract, and to ensure that its student enrollment does not exceed the
28 capacity of its facility or site."

2 Section 14. Section 20-7-1306, MCA, is amended to read:
3 "20-7-1306. (Temporary) Designation of athletic teams. (1) Interscholastic, intercollegiate,
4 intramural, or club athletic teams or sports that are sponsored by a public elementary or high school, a public
5 institution of higher education, or any school or institution whose students or teams compete against a public
6 school or institution of higher education must be expressly designated as one of the following based on
7 biological sex:
8 (a) males, men, or boys;
9 (b) females, women, or girls; or
10 (c) coed or mixed.
11 (2) Athletic teams or sports designated for females, women, or girls may not be open to students of
12 the male sex.
13 (3) For the purposes of this section, "female", "male", and "sex" are defined in 1-1-201 [section 1].
14 (Void on occurrence of contingency--sec. 6, Ch. 405, L. 2021.)"

9 SECTION 17. Section 20-11-116, MCA, is amended to read:
10 "20-11-116. Enrollment. (1) (a) A community choice school must be open to any student residing in
11 the state.
12 (b) A school district may not require a student enrolled in the school district to attend a choice
13 school.
14 (c) A choice school may limit admission to students within a given age group or grade level.
15 (d) A choice school may be organized for a special emphasis, theme, or concept as stated in the
16 school's proposal.
17 (e) A choice school shall enroll all students who wish to attend the school unless the number of
18 students exceeds the capacity of a program, class, grade level, or building.
19 (f) If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend the school, the choice school
20 shall select students through a lottery.
21 (2) A traditional public school converting to a choice school shall adopt and maintain a policy
22 giving enrollment preference to students who reside within the former attendance area of that public school.
23 (3) (a) A choice school shall give enrollment preference to students who were enrolled in the
24 choice school the previous school year and to siblings of students already enrolled in the choice school. An
25 enrollment preference for returning students and siblings excludes those students from entering a lottery.
26 (b) A choice school may give enrollment preference to children of a choice school's employees
27 and governing board, limited to no more than 10% of the school's total student population.
28 (4) This section does not preclude the formation of a community choice school for the purpose of
- 15 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 serving students with disabilities, students of the same gender, as provided in [section 1], students who pose a
2 sufficiently severe disciplinary problem to warrant a specific educational program, or students who are at risk of
3 academic failure. If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend a school, the choice school
4 shall select students through a lottery.
5 (5) If a student who was previously enrolled in a choice school enrolls in any other public school in
6 this state, the student's new school shall accept credits earned by the student in courses or instructional
7 programs at the choice school.
8 (6) A traditional school district shall provide or publicize to parents and the general public
9 information about choice schools as an enrollment option within the district's physical, geographical boundaries
10 to the same extent and through the same means that the district provides and publicizes information about
11 traditional public schools in the district.
12 (7) An authorizer may not restrict the number of students a choice school may enroll. The capacity
13 of the choice school must be determined annually by its governing board in conjunction with the authorizer and
14 in consideration of the choice school's ability to facilitate the academic success of its students, to achieve the
15 objectives specified in the charter contract, and to ensure that its student enrollment does not exceed the
16 capacity of its facility or site.
17 (8) If the choice school is the only public school in a town, the choice school must give preference
18 to enrolling pupils residing in the town or within 5 miles of the school if the next closest public school is more
19 than 10 miles away from the student's residence."

11 SECTION 21. Section 23-2-505, MCA, is amended to read:
12 "23-2-505. Owner's civil liability. The owner of a vessel is liable for any injury or damage
13 occasioned by the negligent operation of the vessel, whether the negligence consists of a violation of the
14 provisions of the statutes of this state or neglecting to observe ordinary care and operation that the rules of the
15 common law require. However, the owner is not liable unless the vessel is being used with the owner's express
16 or implied consent. It must be presumed that the vessel is being operated with the knowledge and consent of
17 the owner if, at the time of the injury or damage, it is under the control of the owner's spouse, father as defined
18 in [section 1], mother as defined in [section 1], brother, sister, son, daughter, or other immediate member of the
19 owner's family. This section may not be construed to relieve any other person from any liability that the person
20 would otherwise have. However, this section may not be construed to authorize or permit any recovery in
21 excess of injury or damage actually incurred."

4 (ii) a working member of a partnership;
5 (iii) a working member of a limited liability partnership;
6 (iv) a working member of a member-managed limited liability company; or
7 (v) a manager of a manager-managed limited liability company that is engaged in the work of the
8 construction industry as defined in 39-71-116.
9 (4) (a) A corporation or a manager-managed limited liability company shall provide coverage for its
10 employees under the provisions of compensation plan No. 1, 2, or 3. A quasi-public corporation, a private
11 corporation, or a manager-managed limited liability company may elect coverage for its corporate officers or
12 managers, who are otherwise exempt under subsection (2), by giving a written notice in the following manner:
13 (i) if the employer has elected to be bound by the provisions of compensation plan No. 1, by
14 delivering the notice to the board of directors of the corporation or to the management organization of the
15 manager-managed limited liability company; or
16 (ii) if the employer has elected to be bound by the provisions of compensation plan No. 2 or 3, by
17 delivering the notice to the board of directors of the corporation or to the management organization of the
18 manager-managed limited liability company and to the insurer.
19 (b) If the employer changes plans or insurers, the employer's previous election is not effective and
20 the employer shall again serve notice to its insurer and to its board of directors or the management organization
21 of the manager-managed limited liability company if the employer elects to be bound.
22 (5) The appointment or election of an employee as an officer of a corporation, a partner in a
23 partnership, a partner in a limited liability partnership, or a member in or a manager of a limited liability
24 company for the purpose of exempting the employee from coverage under this chapter does not entitle the
25 officer, partner, member, or manager to exemption from coverage.
26 (6) Each employer shall post a sign in the workplace at the locations where notices to employees
27 are normally posted, informing employees about the employer's current provision of workers' compensation
28 insurance. A workplace is any location where an employee performs any work-related act in the course of
- 28 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 employment, regardless of whether the location is temporary or permanent, and includes the place of business
2 or property of a third person while the employer has access to or control over the place of business or property
3 for the purpose of carrying on the employer's usual trade, business, or occupation. The sign must be provided
4 by the department, distributed through insurers or directly by the department, and posted by employers in

13 Section 33. Section 40-6-701, MCA, is amended to read:
14 "40-6-701. Interference with fundamental parental rights restricted -- cause of action. (1) A
15 government entity may not interfere with the fundamental right of parents to direct the upbringing, education,
16 health care, and mental health of their children unless the government entity demonstrates that the
17 interference:
18 (a) furthers a compelling governmental interest; and
19 (b) is narrowly tailored and is the least restrictive means available for the furthering of the
20 compelling governmental interest.
21 (2) All fundamental parental rights are exclusively reserved to the parent of a child without
22 obstruction or interference by a government entity, including but not limited to the rights and responsibilities to
23 do the following:
24 (a) direct the education of the child, including the right to choose public, private, religious, or home
25 schools and the right to make reasonable choices with public schools for the education of the child;
26 (b) access and review all written and electronic education records relating to the child that are
27 controlled by or in the possession of a school;
28 (c) direct the upbringing of the child;
- 35 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (d) direct the moral or religious training of the child;
2 (e) make and consent to all physical and mental health care decisions for the child;

4 (g) consent before a biometric scan of the child is made, shared, or stored;
5 (h) consent before a record of the child's blood or DNA is created, stored, or shared, unless
6 authorized pursuant to a court order;
7 (i) consent before a government entity makes an audio or video recording of the child, unless the
8 audio or video recording is made during or as part of:
9 (i) a court proceeding;
10 (ii) a law enforcement investigation;
11 (iii) a forensic interview in a criminal or child abuse and neglect investigation;
12 (iv) the security or surveillance of buildings grounds, or transportation of students; or
13 (v) a photo identification card;
14 (j) be notified promptly if an employee of a government entity suspects that abuse, neglect, or a
15 criminal offense has been committed against the child unless the parent is suspected to have caused the

18 district that would capture data for inclusion in the statewide data system except data that is necessary and
19 essential for establishing a student's education record;

23 (n) be notified promptly if, and provide consent before, the child would share a room or sleeping
24 quarters with an individual of the opposite sex on a school-sponsored trip. A child whose parent does not

13 SECTION 41. Section 46-18-101, MCA, is amended to read:
14 "46-18-101. Correctional and sentencing policy. (1) It is the purpose of this section to establish the
15 correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana. Laws for the punishment of crime are drawn to
16 implement the policy established by this section.
17 (2) The correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana is to:
18 (a) punish each offender commensurate with the nature and degree of harm caused by the offense
19 and to hold an offender accountable;
20 (b) protect the public, reduce crime, and increase the public sense of safety by incarcerating
21 violent offenders and serious repeat offenders;
22 (c) provide restitution, reparation, and restoration to the victim of the offense; and
23 (d) encourage and provide opportunities for the offender's self-improvement to provide
24 rehabilitation and reintegration of offenders back into the community.
25 (3) To achieve the policy outlined in subsection (2), the state of Montana adopts the following
26 principles:
27 (a) Sentencing and punishment must be certain, timely, consistent, and understandable.
28 (b) Sentences should be commensurate with the punishment imposed on other persons
- 53 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 committing the same offenses.
2 (c) Sentencing practices must be neutral with respect to the offender's race, gender, as provided in
3 [section 1], religion, national origin, or social or economic status.
4 (d) Sentencing practices must permit judicial discretion to consider aggravating and mitigating
5 circumstances.
6 (e) Sentencing practices must include punishing violent and serious repeat felony offenders with
7 incarceration.
8 (f) Sentencing practices must provide alternatives to imprisonment for the punishment of those
9 nonviolent felony offenders who do not have serious criminal records.
10 (g) Sentencing and correctional practices must emphasize that the offender is responsible for
11 obeying the law and must hold the offender accountable for the offender's actions.
12 (h) Sentencing practices must emphasize restitution to the victim by the offender. A sentence must
13 require an offender who is financially able to do so to pay restitution, costs as provided in 46-18-232, costs of
14 assigned counsel, as provided in 46-8-113, and, if the offender is a sex offender, costs of any chemical
15 treatment.
16 (i) Sentencing practices should promote and support practices, policies, and programs that focus
17 on restorative justice principles."
18
19 Section 42. Section 46-19-301, MCA, is amended to read:
20 "46-19-301. Western Interstate Corrections Compact -- contents. The Western Interstate
21 Corrections Compact as contained herein is hereby enacted into law and entered into on behalf of this state
22 with any and all other states legally joining therein in a form substantially as follows:
23 WESTERN INTERSTATE CORRECTIONS COMPACT
24 ARTICLE I
25 PURPOSE AND POLICY
26 The party states, desiring by common action to improve their institutional facilities and provide
27 programs of sufficiently high quality for the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of various types of
28 offenders, declare that it is the policy of each of the party states to provide such facilities and programs on the
- 54 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 basis of cooperation with one another, thereby serving the best interests of such offenders and of society. The
2 purpose of this compact is to provide for the development and execution of such programs of cooperation for
3 the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of offenders.
4 ARTICLE II
5 DEFINITIONS
6 As used in this compact, unless the context clearly requires otherwise:
7 (1) "state" means a state of the United States or, subject to the limitation contained in Article VII,
8 Guam;
9 (2) "sending state" means a state party to this compact in which conviction was had;
10 (3) "receiving state" means a state party to this compact to which an inmate is sent for confinement
11 other than a state in which conviction was had;
12 (4) "inmate" means a male or female, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], offender who is under
13 sentence to or confined in a prison or other correctional institution;
14 (5) "institution" means any prison, reformatory, or other correctional facility (including but not
15 limited to a facility for the mentally ill or mentally defective) in which inmates may lawfully be confined.
16 ARTICLE III
17 CONTRACTS
18 (1) Each party state may make one or more contracts with any one or more of the other party
19 states for the confinement of inmates on behalf of a sending state in institutions situated within receiving states.
20 Any such contract shall provide for:
21 (a) its duration;
22 (b) payments to be made to the receiving state by the sending state for inmate maintenance,
23 extraordinary medical and dental expenses, and any participation in or receipt by inmates of rehabilitative or
24 correctional services, facilities, programs, or treatment not reasonably included as part of normal maintenance;
25 (c) participation in programs of inmate employment, if any; the disposition or crediting of any
26 payments received by inmates on account thereof; and the crediting of proceeds from or disposal of any
27 products resulting therefrom;
28 (d) delivery and retaking of inmates;
- 55 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (e) such other matters as may be necessary and appropriate to fix the obligations, responsibilities,
2 and rights of the sending and receiving states.
3 (2) Prior to the construction or completion of construction of any institution or addition thereto by a
4 party state, any other party state or states may contract therewith for the enlargement of the planned capacity
5 of the institution or addition thereto, or for the inclusion therein of particular equipment or structures, and for the
6 reservation of a specific percent of the capacity of the institution to be kept available for use by inmates of the
7 sending state or states so contracting. Any sending state so contracting may, to the extent that moneys are
8 legally available therefor, pay to the receiving state a reasonable sum as consideration for such enlargement of
9 capacity or provision of equipment or structures and reservation of capacity. Such payment may be in a lump
10 sum or in installments as provided in the contract.
11 (3) The terms and provisions of this compact shall be a part of any contract entered into by the
12 authority of or pursuant thereto, and nothing in any such contract shall be inconsistent therewith.
13 ARTICLE IV
14 PROCEDURES AND RIGHTS
15 (1) Whenever the duly constituted judicial or administrative authorities in a state party to this
16 compact, and which has entered into a contract pursuant to Article III, shall decide that confinement in or
17 transfer of an inmate to an institution within the territory of another party state is necessary in order to provide
18 adequate quarters and care or desirable in order to provide an appropriate program of rehabilitation or
19 treatment, said officials may direct that the confinement be within an institution within the territory of said other
20 party state, the receiving state to act in that regard solely as agent for the sending state.
21 (2) The appropriate officials of any state party to this compact shall have access at all reasonable
22 times to any institution in which it has a contractual right to confine inmates for the purpose of inspecting the
23 facilities thereof and visiting such of its inmates as may be confined in the institution.
24 (3) Inmates confined in an institution pursuant to the terms of this compact shall at all times be
25 subject to the jurisdiction of the sending state and may at any time be removed therefrom for transfer to a
26 prison or other institution within the sending state, for transfer to another institution in which the sending state
27 may have a contractual or other right to confine inmates, for release on probation or parole, for discharge, or for
28 any other purpose permitted by the laws of the sending state; provided that the sending state shall continue to
- 56 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 be obligated to such payments as may be required pursuant to the terms of any contract entered into under the
2 terms of Article III.
3 (4) Each receiving state shall provide regular reports to each sending state on the inmates of that
4 sending state in institutions pursuant to this compact including a conduct record of each inmate and certify said
5 record to the official designated by the sending state in order that each inmate may have the benefit of the
6 inmate's record in determining and altering the disposition of said inmate in accordance with the law which may
7 obtain in the sending state and in order that the same may be a source of information for the sending state.
8 (5) All inmates who may be confined in an institution pursuant to the provisions of this compact
9 shall be treated in a reasonable and humane manner and shall be cared for and treated equally with such
10 similar inmates of the receiving state as may be confined in the same institution. The fact of confinement in a
11 receiving state shall not deprive any inmate so confined of any legal rights which said inmate would have had if
12 confined in an appropriate institution of the sending state.
13 (6) Any hearing or hearings to which an inmate confined pursuant to this compact may be entitled
14 by the laws of the sending state may be had before the appropriate authorities of the sending state or of the
15 receiving state if authorized by the sending state. The receiving state shall provide adequate facilities for such
16 hearings as may be conducted by the appropriate officials of a sending state. In the event such hearing or
17 hearings are had before officials of the receiving state, the governing law shall be that of the sending state and
18 a record of the hearing or hearings as prescribed by the sending state shall be made. Said record together with
19 any recommendations of the hearing officials shall be transmitted forthwith to the official or officials before
20 whom the hearing would have been had if it had taken place in the sending state. In any and all proceedings
21 had pursuant to the provisions of this subdivision, the officials of the receiving state shall act solely as agents of
22 the sending state and no final determination shall be made in any matter except by the appropriate officials of
23 the sending state. Costs of records made pursuant to this subsection shall be borne by the sending state.
24 (7) Any inmate confined pursuant to this compact shall be released within the territory of the
25 sending state unless the inmate and the sending and receiving states shall agree upon release in some other
26 place. The sending state shall bear the cost of such return to its territory.
27 (8) Any inmate confined pursuant to the terms of this compact shall have any and all rights to
28 participate in and derive any benefits, incur or be relieved of any obligations, or have such obligations modified
- 57 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 or the inmate's status changed on account of any action or proceeding in which the inmate could have
2 participated if confined in any appropriate institution of the sending state located within such state.
3 (9) The parent, guardian, trustee, or other person or persons entitled under the laws of the sending
4 state to act for, advise, or otherwise function with respect to any inmate shall not be deprived of or restricted in
5 the person's exercise of any power in respect of any inmate confined pursuant to the terms of this compact.
6 ARTICLE V
7 ACTS NOT REVIEWABLE IN RECEIVING STATE -- EXTRADITION
8 (1) Any decision of the sending state in respect of any matter over which it retains jurisdiction
9 pursuant to this compact shall be conclusive upon and not reviewable within the receiving state, but if at the
10 time the sending state seeks to remove an inmate from an institution in the receiving state there is pending
11 against the inmate within such state any criminal charge or if the inmate is suspected of having committed
12 within such state a criminal offense, the inmate shall not be returned without the consent of the receiving state
13 until discharged from prosecution or other form of proceeding, imprisonment, or detention for such offense. The
14 duly accredited officers of the sending state shall be permitted to transport inmates pursuant to this compact
15 through any and all states party to this compact without interference.
16 (2) An inmate who escapes from an institution in which the inmate is confined pursuant to this
17 compact shall be deemed a fugitive from the sending state and from the state in which the institution is situated.
18 In the case of an escape to a jurisdiction other than the sending or receiving state, the responsibility for
19 institution of extradition proceedings shall be that of the sending state, but nothing contained herein shall be
20 construed to prevent or affect the activities of officers and agencies of any jurisdiction directed toward the
21 apprehension and return of an escapee.
22 ARTICLE VI
23 FEDERAL AID
24 Any state party to this compact may accept federal aid for use in connection with any institution or
25 program, the use of which is or may be affected by this compact or any contract pursuant hereto, and any
26 inmate in a receiving state pursuant to this compact may participate in any such federally aided program or
27 activity for which the sending and receiving states have made contractual provision, provided that, if such
28 program or activity is not part of the customary correctional regimen, the express consent of the appropriate
- 58 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 official of the sending state shall be required therefor.
2 ARTICLE VII
3 ENTRY INTO FORCE
4 This compact shall enter into force and become effective and binding upon the states so acting when it
5 has been enacted into law by any two contiguous states from among the states of Alaska, Arizona, California,
6 Colorado, Hawaii, Idaho, Montana, Nebraska, Nevada, New Mexico, Oregon, Utah, Washington, and Wyoming.
7 For the purposes of this article, Alaska and Hawaii shall be deemed contiguous to each other; to any and all of
8 the states of California, Oregon, and Washington; and to Guam. Thereafter, this compact shall enter into force
9 and become effective and binding as to any other of said states or any other state contiguous to at least one
10 party state upon similar action by such state. Guam may become party to this compact by taking action similar
11 to that provided for joinder by any other eligible party state and upon the consent of congress to such joinder.
12 For the purposes of this article, Guam shall be deemed contiguous to Alaska, Hawaii, California, Oregon, and
13 Washington.
14 ARTICLE VIII
15 WITHDRAWAL AND TERMINATION
16 This compact shall continue in force and remain binding upon a party state until it shall have enacted a
17 statute repealing the same and providing for the sending of formal written notice of withdrawal from the
18 compact to the appropriate officials of all other party states. An actual withdrawal shall not take effect until 2
19 years after the notices provided in said statute have been sent. Such withdrawal shall not relieve the
20 withdrawing state from its obligations assumed hereunder prior to the effective date of withdrawal. Before the
21 effective date of withdrawal, a withdrawing state shall remove to its territory, at its own expense, such inmates
22 as it may have confined pursuant to the provisions of this compact.
23 ARTICLE IX
24 OTHER ARRANGEMENTS UNAFFECTED
25 Nothing contained in this compact shall be construed to abrogate or impair any agreement or other
26 arrangement which a party state may have with a nonparty state for the confinement, rehabilitation, or
27 treatment of inmates or to repeal any other laws of a party state authorizing the making of cooperative
28 institutional arrangements.
- 59 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 ARTICLE X
2 CONSTRUCTION AND SEVERABILITY
3 The provisions of this compact shall be liberally construed and shall be severable. If any phrase,
4 clause, sentence, or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of any participating
5 state or of the United States or the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person, or circumstance is
6 held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact and the applicability thereof to any government,
7 agency, person, or circumstance shall not be affected thereby. If this compact shall be held contrary to the
8 constitution of any state participating therein, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the
9 remaining states and in full force and effect as to the state affected as to all severable matters."

11 Section 43. Section 46-19-401, MCA, is amended to read:
12 "46-19-401. Compact adopted -- text. The Interstate Corrections Compact is entered into by this
13 state with any and all other states legally joining therein in the form substantially as follows:
14 INTERSTATE CORRECTIONS COMPACT
15 ARTICLE I
16 PURPOSE AND POLICY
17 The party states, desiring by common action to fully utilize and improve their institutional facilities and
18 provide adequate programs for the confinement, treatment and rehabilitation of various types of offenders,
19 declare that it is the policy of each of the party states to provide such facilities and programs on a basis of
20 cooperation with one another, thereby serving the best interests of such offenders and of society and effecting
21 economies in capital expenditures and operational costs. The purpose of this compact is to provide for the
22 mutual development and execution of such programs of cooperation for the confinement, treatment and
23 rehabilitation of offenders with the most economical use of human and material resources.
24 ARTICLE II
25 DEFINITIONS
26 As used in this compact, unless the context requires otherwise:
27 (a) "State" means a state of the United States; the United States of America; a territory or
28 possession of the United States; the District of Columbia; the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico.

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (b) "Sending state" means a state party to this compact in which conviction or court commitment
2 was had.

4 confinement other than a state in which conviction or court commitment was had.
5 (d) "Inmate" means a male or female, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], offender who is committed
6 under sentence to or confined in a penal or correctional institution.
7 (e) "Institution" means any penal or correctional facility, including but not limited to a facility for the
8 mentally ill or mentally defective, in which inmates may lawfully be confined.

8 Section 48. Section 50-5-105, MCA, is amended to read:
9 "50-5-105. Discrimination prohibited. (1) All phases of the operation of a health care facility must be
10 without discrimination against anyone on the basis of race, creed, religion, color, national origin, sex, as defined
11 in 1-1-201 [section 1], age, marital status, physical or mental disability, or political ideas.
12 (2) (a) A health care facility may not refuse to admit a person to the facility solely because the
13 person has an HIV-related condition.
14 (b) For the purposes of this subsection (2), the following definitions apply:
15 (i) "HIV" means the human immunodeficiency virus identified as the causative agent of acquired
16 immunodeficiency syndrome (AIDS) and includes all HIV and HIV-related viruses that damage the cellular
17 branch of the human immune or neurological system and leave the infected person immunodeficient or
18 neurologically impaired.
19 (ii) "HIV-related condition" means any medical condition resulting from an HIV infection, including
20 but not limited to seropositivity for HIV.
21 (3) A person who operates a facility may not discriminate among the patients of licensed
22 physicians. The free and confidential professional relationship between a licensed physician and patient must
23 continue and remain unaffected.
24 (4) Except for a hospital that employs its medical staff, a hospital considering an application for
25 staff membership or granting privileges within the scope of the applicant's license may not deny the application
26 or privileges because the applicant is licensed under Title 37, chapter 6."

25 worker, clinical professional counselor, marriage and family therapist, addiction counselor, or another
26 appropriate licensed health care practitioner.
27 (9) "Recovery residence" means a sober living home with a safe, family-like environment that
28 promotes recovery from substance use disorders through services including but not limited to peer support,
- 84 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 mutual support groups, and recovery services.
2 (10) "Sober" means free of alcohol and drugs, except for prescription medications taken as directed
3 by a licensed prescriber, including medications approved by the United States food and drug administration for
4 the treatment of opioid use disorder.
5 (11) (a) "Substance use disorder" means the use of any chemical substance, legal or illegal, that
6 creates behavioral or health problems, or both, resulting in operational impairment.
7 (b) This term includes alcoholism, drug dependency, or both, that endanger the health,
8 interpersonal relationships, or economic functions of an individual or the public health, safety, or welfare."

10 SECTION 59. Section 53-30-312, MCA, is amended to read:
11 "53-30-312. Creation of community corrections boards -- membership -- appointment -- terms --
12 compensation. (1) A unit of local government, the governing bodies of two or more units of local government,
13 or a tribal government may establish a community corrections board.
14 (2) A community corrections board consists of three to seven members, must, when possible, be
15 gender-balanced, as provided in [section 1], and have racial parity, and must include:
16 (a) one local law enforcement officer;
17 (b) one probation and parole officer; and
18 (c) one member of the public.
19 (3) Members of a community corrections board must be appointed by the chief executive officer of
20 the unit of local government or the tribal government in the judicial district in which community corrections
21 facilities or programs are established.
22 (4) Members of a community corrections board shall serve for a term of 4 years.
23 (5) Members of a community corrections board shall serve without compensation except as
24 otherwise decided by the units of local government or a tribal government."

27 of physical exercise, collective amusement, or enjoyment of nature. Such activities may include hiking, golfing,

9 Section 63. Section 72-1-103, MCA, is amended to read:

17 appointment under chapter 3, part 2.
18 (3) "Beneficiary", as it relates to:
19 (a) a trust beneficiary, includes a person who has any present or future interest, vested or

23 (i) an account with POD designation or a security registered in beneficiary form (TOD); or
24 (ii) any other nonprobate transfer at death; and

26 trust beneficiary, a beneficiary of a beneficiary designation, a donee, and a person in whose favor a power of

- 89 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2

4 succession from the parent whose relationship is involved and excludes a person who is only a stepchild, a
5 foster child, a grandchild, or any more remote descendant.

7 decedent or protected person, whether arising in contract, in tort, or otherwise, and liabilities of the estate that

14 person.
15 (9) "Court" means the district court in this state having jurisdiction in matters relating to the affairs
16 of decedents.
17 (10) "Descendant" of an individual means all of the individual's descendants of all generations, with
18 the relationship of parent and child at each generation being determined by the definition of child and parent
19 contained in this code.

18 SECTION 64. Section 72-17-106, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "72-17-106. Statewide organ and tissue donation registry. (1) The department of justice shall
20 electronically transfer to the federally designated organ procurement organization all information that appears
21 on the front of a driver's license, including the name, gender, as provided in [section 1], date of birth, and most
22 recent address of any person who obtains a driver's license and who volunteers to donate organs or tissue
23 upon death, as provided in 61-5-301. The department of justice may charge actual costs for the first transfer of
24 information, as provided in subsection (5). However, all subsequent electronic transfers of donor information
25 must be at no charge to the federally designated organ procurement organization.
26 (2) Information obtained by the federally designated organ procurement organization must be used
27 for the purpose of establishing a statewide organ and tissue donation registry accessible to in-state, recognized
28 cadaveric organ and cadaveric tissue agencies for the recovery or placement of organs and tissue and to
- 94 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 procurement agencies in another state when a Montana resident is a donor of an anatomical gift and is not
2 located in the state at the time of death or immediately before the death of the donor.
3 (3) An organ or tissue donation organization may not obtain information from the organ and tissue
4 donation registry for the purpose of fundraising. Organ and tissue donation registry information may not be
5 further disseminated unless authorized in this section or by federal law. Dissemination of organ and tissue
6 donation registry information may be made by the organ procurement organization to a recognized, in-state
7 procurement agency for other tissue recovery or to an out-of-state, federally designated organ procurement
8 organization.
9 (4) The federally designated organ procurement organization may acquire donor information from
10 sources other than the department of justice.
11 (5) All reasonable costs associated with the creation and maintenance of the organ and tissue
12 donation registry, as determined by the department of justice, must be paid by the organ and tissue
13 procurement organizations. Any money collected by the department of justice must be deposited in an account
14 in the state special revenue fund established by the department of justice for the purpose of the payment of
15 reasonable costs associated with the development and maintenance of the organ and tissue donation registry
16 and necessary for the initial installation and setup for electronic transfer of the donor information.
17 (6) An individual does not need to participate in the organ and tissue donation registry to be a
18 donor of organs or tissue. The registry is intended to facilitate organ and tissue donation and not inhibit persons
19 from being donors upon death."

14 NEW SECTION. Section 66. Repealer. The following section of the Montana Code Annotated is
15 repealed:
16 1-1-201. Terms of wide applicability.
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 67. Codification instruction. [Section 1] is intended to be codified as an
19 integral part of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, and the provisions of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, apply to [section 1].
20
21 NEW SECTION. Section 68. Severability. If a part of [this act] is invalid, all valid parts that are
22 severable from the invalid part remain in effect. If a part of [this act] is invalid in one or more of its applications,
23 the part remains in effect in all valid applications that are severable from the invalid applications.
24
25 NEW SECTION. Section 69. Effective date. [This act] is effective on passage and approval.

Raw Text:
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 SENATE BILL NO. 437
2 INTRODUCED BY C. GLIMM
3
4 A BILL FOR AN ACT ENTITLED: “AN ACT FOR THE CODIFICATION AND GENERAL REVISION OF THE
5 LAWS RELATING TO THE DEFINITION FOR THE WORDS SEX, FEMALE, AND MALE, MAN, WOMAN,
6 FATHER, AND MOTHER WHEN REFERRING TO A HUMAN; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX
7 REFERS TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT GENDER IDENTITY OR SEXUAL INTERCOURSE; PROVIDING
8 THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX IS LIMITED TO TWO TYPES OF SEXES WHICH ARE REFERRED TO AS
9 MALE AND FEMALE; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITIONS OF MALE, AND FEMALE, MAN, WOMAN,
10 FATHER, AND MOTHER REFER TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT SUBJECTIVE GENDER IDENTITY;
11 CLARIFYING THE MEANING OF THE TERM "GENDER"; AMENDING SECTIONS 2-18-208, 2-18-606, 7-15-
12 4207, 7-34-2123, 10-2-403, 13-27-408, 13-35-301, 13-38-201, 13-38-203, 13-38-205, 19-2-802, 20-6-808, 20-
13 7-1306, 20-7-1703, 20-9-327, 20-11-116, 20-25-501, 20-25-707, 22-2-306, 23-2-505, 33-1-201, 35-20-209, 39-
14 2-912, 39-29-101, 39-71-401, 40-1-107, 40-1-311, 40-1-401, 40-5-804, 40-5-907, 40-5-1031, 40-6-701, 40-6-
15 703, 41-3-210, 41-5-103, 42-2-204, 44-2-411, 44-2-412, 45-5-625, 46-18-101, 46-19-301, 46-19-401, 49-1-102,
16 49-2-101, 49-3-101, 50-4-720, 50-5-105, 50-5-602, 50-11-101, 50-15-101, 50-19-103, 50-19-501, 50-60-214,
17 53-20-142, 53-21-121, 53-21-142, 53-24-310, 53-30-312, 60-5-514, 60-5-522, 61-5-107, 72-1-103, 72-17-106,
18 AND 90-14-104, MCA; REPEALING SECTION 1-1-201, MCA; AND PROVIDING AN IMMEDIATE EFFECTIVE
19 DATE.”
20
21 WHEREAS, in human beings, there are two -- and only two -- sexes: male and female, which refer to
22 the two body structures (phenotypes) that, in normal development, correspond to one or the other gamete --
23 sperm for males and ova for females; and
24 WHEREAS, every individual is either male or female; and
25 WHEREAS, an individual's sex can be observed or clinically verified at or before birth; and
26 WHEREAS, rare disorders of sexual development are not exceptions to the binary nature of sex; and
27
28 WHEREAS, in no case is an individual's sex determined by stipulation or self-identification; and
- 1 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 WHEREAS, there is increasing confusion about the definition and implications of sex as a biological
2 truth and its relationship to concepts and terms including but not limited to sex assigned at birth, gender, gender
3 identity, gender role, gender expression, and experienced gender; and
4 WHEREAS, confusion and ambiguities surrounding the definitions of sex, male, female, and related
5 terms can hinder individual efforts to enjoy equal treatment under the law; and
6 WHEREAS, legal equality of the two sexes -- male and female -- does not imply that the sexes are
7 identical to each other or are the same in every respect; and
8 WHEREAS, with respect to the two sexes -- male and female -- separate facilities or sports leagues
9 established because of or organized according to physical differences between the sexes do not constitute
10 unequal treatment under the law; and
11 WHEREAS, physical differences between males and females are enduring, and the two sexes are not
12 fungible.
13 THEREFORE, it is the intent of the Legislature of this state to clarify and reconcile the meaning of sex,
14 male, female, and related terms in state laws, administrative rules, and guidelines.
15
16 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF THE STATE OF MONTANA:
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 1. Terms of wide applicability. (1) Unless the context requires otherwise,
19 the following definitions apply in the Montana Code Annotated:
20 (a) "FATHER" MEANS A MALE PARENT.
21 (B) "Female" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XX
22 chromosomes and produces or would produce relatively large, relatively immobile gametes, or eggs, during her
23 life cycle and has a reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An
24 individual who would otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is female, WHEN
25 USED TO REFER TO A NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT
26 FOR A CONGENITAL ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT
27 SOME POINT PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE LARGE GAMETE, OR OVA, FOR FERTILIZATION.
28 (b) (C) "Male" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XY
- 2 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 chromosomes and produces or would produce small, mobile gametes, or sperm, during his life cycle and has a
2 reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An individual who would
3 otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is male, WHEN USED TO REFER TO A
4 NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT FOR A CONGENITAL
5 ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT SOME POINT
6 PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE SMALL GAMETE, OR SPERM, FOR FERTILIZATION.
7 (c) (D) "MAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN MALE, EXCEPT WHEN USED AS A GENERIC REFERENCE TO HUMAN
8 BEINGS.
9 (E) "MOTHER" MEANS A FEMALE PARENT.
10 (F) "Oath" includes an affirmation or declaration.
11 (d) (G) "Person" includes a corporation or other entity as well as a natural person.
12 (e) (H) "Several" means two or more.
13 (f) (I) "Sex" means the organization of the body parts and gametes for reproduction in human beings
14 and other organisms. In human beings, there are exactly two sexes, male and female, with two corresponding
15 types of gametes. The sexes are determined by the biological and genetic indication of male or female,
16 including sex chromosomes, naturally occurring sex chromosomes, gonads, and nonambiguous internal and
17 external genitalia present at birth, without regard to an individual's psychological, behavioral, social, chosen, or
18 subjective experience of gender WHETHER SOMEONE IS MALE OR FEMALE, WHICH IS DISTINGUISHED BASED ON THE
19 TYPE OF GAMETE, SPERM OR EGGS, THEY ARE CAPABLE OF OR EXPECTED TO PRODUCE, AS DICTATED BY THEIR PRIMARY
20 SEXUAL ANATOMY. BECAUSE THERE ARE ONLY TWO TYPES OF GAMETES, SPERM AND OVA, WITH TWO CORRESPONDING
21 REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEMS, THERE ARE ONLY TWO SEXES: MALE AND FEMALE. AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX IS ROOTED IN
22 REPRODUCTIVE ANATOMY AND IS IN NO WAY INFLUENCED OR DEFINED BY ONE'S PSYCHOLOGICAL STATE, BEHAVIOR,
23 EXPRESSION, OR PERSONAL IDENTITY.
24 (g) (J) "State", when applied to the different parts of the United States, includes the District of
25 Columbia and the territories.
26 (h) (K) "United States" includes the District of Columbia and the territories.
27 (L) "WOMAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN FEMALE.
28 (2) Wherever the word "man" or "men" or a word that includes the syllable "man" or "men" in
- 3 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 combination with other syllables, such as "workman", appears in this code, the word or syllable includes
2 "woman" or "women" unless the context clearly indicates a contrary intent and unless the subject matter of the
3 statute relates clearly and necessarily to a specific sex only.
4 (3) Whenever the term "heretofore" occurs in any statute, it must be construed to mean any time
5 previous to the day the statute takes effect. Whenever the word "hereafter" occurs, it must be construed to
6 mean the time after the statute containing the term takes effect.
7 (4) (A) THE TERM "GENDER", WHEN USED ALONE TO REFER TO A MALE, FEMALE, OR THE NATURAL
8 DIFFERENCES BETWEEN A MALE AND FEMALE:
9 (I) MUST BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM FOR SEX; AND
10 (II) MAY NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SHORT-HAND EXPRESSION FOR GENDER IDENTITY,
11 EXPERIENCED GENDER, GENDER EXPRESSION, OR GENDER ROLE.
12 (B) THE TERM "GENDER" DOES NOT APPLY WHEN IT IS USED IN CONJUNCTION WITH OTHER WORDS OR AS
13 AN ADJECTIVE TO MODIFY OTHER WORDS, OR WHEN CONTEXT OR EXPLICIT DEFINITION IN PREEXISTING STATE LAW,
14 ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES INDICATES OTHERWISE.
15 (C) THE TERM "GENDER IDENTITY", IF USED IN STATE LAW, ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES, MAY
16 NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SUBSTITUTE FOR SEX OR GENDER.
17
18 Section 2. Section 2-18-208, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "2-18-208. Comparable worth. The department of administration shall, in its continuous efforts to
20 enhance the current classification plan and pay schedules, work toward the goal of establishing a standard of
21 equal pay for comparable worth. This standard for the classification plan shall be reached by:
22 (1) eliminating, in the classification of positions, the use of judgments and factors that contain
23 inherent biases based on sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1]; and
24 (2) comparing, in the classification of positions, the factors for determining job worth across
25 occupational groups whenever those groups are dominated by males or females."
26
27 SECTION 3. Section 2-18-606, MCA, is amended to read:
28 "2-18-606. Parental leave for state employees. (1) The department of administration shall develop a
- 4 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 parental leave policy for permanent state employees. The policy must permit an employee to take a reasonable
2 leave of absence and permit the employee to use sick leave immediately following the birth or placement of a
3 child for a period not to exceed 15 working days if:
4 (a) the employee is adopting a child; or
5 (b) the employee is a birth father, as defined in [section 1].

16 Section 8. Section 13-35-301, MCA, is amended to read:
17 "13-35-301. Adoption of code of fair campaign practices. The following code of fair campaign
18 practices is adopted by Montana:
19 "There are basic principles of decency, honesty, and fair play that every candidate for public office in
20 the United States has a moral obligation to observe and uphold, in order that, after vigorously contested but
21 fairly conducted campaigns, our citizens may exercise their constitutional right to a free and untrammeled
22 choice and the will of the people may be fully and clearly expressed on the issues before the country.
23 Therefore:
24 I will conduct my campaign in the best American tradition, discussing the issues as I see them,
25 presenting my record and policies with sincerity and frankness, and criticizing without fear or favor the record
26 and policies of my opponent and my opponent's party that merit such criticism.
27 I will defend and uphold the right of every qualified American voter to full and equal participation in the
28 electoral process.
- 6 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 I will conduct my campaign without the use of personal vilification, character defamation, whispering
2 campaigns, libel, slander, or scurrilous attacks on my opposition or my opposition's personal or family life.
3 I will not use campaign material of any sort that misrepresents, distorts, or otherwise falsifies the facts,
4 nor will I use malicious or unfounded accusations that aim at creating or exploiting doubts, without justification,
5 as to the loyalty and patriotism of my opposition.
6 I will not make any appeal to prejudice based on race, sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], creed, or
7 national origin.
8 I will not undertake or condone any dishonest or unethical practice that tends to corrupt or undermine
9 our American system of free elections or that hampers or prevents the full and free expression of the will of the
10 voters.
11 Insofar as is possible, I will immediately and publicly repudiate support deriving from any individual or
12 group that resorts, on behalf of my candidacy or in opposition to that of my opponent, to the methods and
13 tactics that I have pledged not to use or condone.""
