21 SECTION 13. Section 20-6-808, MCA, is amended to read:
22 "20-6-808. Enrollment. (1) (a) A public charter school must be open to any student residing in the
23 state.
24 (b) A school district may not require a student enrolled in the school district to attend a public
25 charter school.
26 (c) A public charter school may limit admission to students within a given age group or grade level.
27 (d) A public charter school may be organized for a special emphasis, theme, or concept as stated
28 in the school's proposal.
- 10 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (e) A public charter school shall enroll all students who wish to attend the school unless the
2 number of students exceeds the capacity of a program, class, grade level, or building.
3 (f) If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend the school, the public charter
4 school shall select students through a lottery.
5 (2) (a) A public charter school shall give enrollment preference to students who are residents of the
6 located school district.
7 (b) A public charter school may give enrollment preference to:
8 (i) students who were enrolled in the public charter school the previous school year and to siblings
9 of students already enrolled in the public charter school. An enrollment preference for returning students
10 excludes those students from entering a lottery.
11 (ii) children of members of a public charter school's governing board and full-time employees,
12 limited to no more than 10% of the school's total student population.
13 (3) This section does not preclude the formation of a public charter school for the purpose of
14 serving students with disabilities, students of the same gender, as provided in [section 1], students who pose a
15 sufficiently severe disciplinary problem to warrant a specific educational program, or students who are at risk of
16 academic failure. If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend such a school, the public
17 charter school shall select students through a lottery.
18 (4) If a student who was previously enrolled in a public charter school enrolls in any other public
19 school in this state, the student's new school shall accept credits earned by the student in courses or
20 instructional programs at the public charter school.
21 (5) A school district shall provide or publicize to parents and the general public information about
22 public charter schools as an enrollment option within the district to the same extent and through the same
23 means that the district provides and publicizes information about noncharter public schools in the district.
24 (6) The board of public education may not restrict the number of students a public charter school
25 may enroll. The capacity of the public charter school must be determined annually by the governing board in
26 consideration of the public charter school's ability to facilitate the academic success of its students, to achieve
27 the objectives specified in the charter contract, and to ensure that its student enrollment does not exceed the

9 related to the grant."

11 SECTION 21. Section 23-2-505, MCA, is amended to read:
12 "23-2-505. Owner's civil liability. The owner of a vessel is liable for any injury or damage
13 occasioned by the negligent operation of the vessel, whether the negligence consists of a violation of the
14 provisions of the statutes of this state or neglecting to observe ordinary care and operation that the rules of the
15 common law require. However, the owner is not liable unless the vessel is being used with the owner's express
16 or implied consent. It must be presumed that the vessel is being operated with the knowledge and consent of
17 the owner if, at the time of the injury or damage, it is under the control of the owner's spouse, father as defined
18 in [section 1], mother as defined in [section 1], brother, sister, son, daughter, or other immediate member of the
19 owner's family. This section may not be construed to relieve any other person from any liability that the person
20 would otherwise have. However, this section may not be construed to authorize or permit any recovery in
21 excess of injury or damage actually incurred."

25 (h) the name and county of the judicial district or the name and address of the agency where the
26 record of the case is located and the cause number or case identification number for the case.
27 (4) (a) For each IV-D case with a support order registered in the case registry, there must be a

13 Section 33. Section 40-6-701, MCA, is amended to read:
14 "40-6-701. Interference with fundamental parental rights restricted -- cause of action. (1) A
15 government entity may not interfere with the fundamental right of parents to direct the upbringing, education,
16 health care, and mental health of their children unless the government entity demonstrates that the
17 interference:
18 (a) furthers a compelling governmental interest; and
19 (b) is narrowly tailored and is the least restrictive means available for the furthering of the
20 compelling governmental interest.
21 (2) All fundamental parental rights are exclusively reserved to the parent of a child without
22 obstruction or interference by a government entity, including but not limited to the rights and responsibilities to
23 do the following:
24 (a) direct the education of the child, including the right to choose public, private, religious, or home
25 schools and the right to make reasonable choices with public schools for the education of the child;
26 (b) access and review all written and electronic education records relating to the child that are
27 controlled by or in the possession of a school;
28 (c) direct the upbringing of the child;

12 to notice of termination of parental rights proceedings for the purposes of adoption if the putative father has
13 complied with the requirements of the putative father registry.
14 (3) An individual who is not married to the mother but who is presumed to be a father under 40-6-
15 105 and registers in accordance with this part is entitled to receive notice of a termination of parental rights
16 proceeding."

13 SECTION 41. Section 46-18-101, MCA, is amended to read:
14 "46-18-101. Correctional and sentencing policy. (1) It is the purpose of this section to establish the
15 correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana. Laws for the punishment of crime are drawn to
16 implement the policy established by this section.
17 (2) The correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana is to:
18 (a) punish each offender commensurate with the nature and degree of harm caused by the offense
19 and to hold an offender accountable;
20 (b) protect the public, reduce crime, and increase the public sense of safety by incarcerating
21 violent offenders and serious repeat offenders;
22 (c) provide restitution, reparation, and restoration to the victim of the offense; and
23 (d) encourage and provide opportunities for the offender's self-improvement to provide
24 rehabilitation and reintegration of offenders back into the community.
25 (3) To achieve the policy outlined in subsection (2), the state of Montana adopts the following
26 principles:
27 (a) Sentencing and punishment must be certain, timely, consistent, and understandable.
28 (b) Sentences should be commensurate with the punishment imposed on other persons
- 53 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 committing the same offenses.
2 (c) Sentencing practices must be neutral with respect to the offender's race, gender, as provided in
3 [section 1], religion, national origin, or social or economic status.
4 (d) Sentencing practices must permit judicial discretion to consider aggravating and mitigating
5 circumstances.
6 (e) Sentencing practices must include punishing violent and serious repeat felony offenders with
7 incarceration.
8 (f) Sentencing practices must provide alternatives to imprisonment for the punishment of those
9 nonviolent felony offenders who do not have serious criminal records.
10 (g) Sentencing and correctional practices must emphasize that the offender is responsible for
11 obeying the law and must hold the offender accountable for the offender's actions.
12 (h) Sentencing practices must emphasize restitution to the victim by the offender. A sentence must
13 require an offender who is financially able to do so to pay restitution, costs as provided in 46-18-232, costs of
14 assigned counsel, as provided in 46-8-113, and, if the offender is a sex offender, costs of any chemical
15 treatment.
16 (i) Sentencing practices should promote and support practices, policies, and programs that focus
17 on restorative justice principles."
18
19 Section 42. Section 46-19-301, MCA, is amended to read:
20 "46-19-301. Western Interstate Corrections Compact -- contents. The Western Interstate
21 Corrections Compact as contained herein is hereby enacted into law and entered into on behalf of this state
22 with any and all other states legally joining therein in a form substantially as follows:
23 WESTERN INTERSTATE CORRECTIONS COMPACT
24 ARTICLE I
25 PURPOSE AND POLICY
26 The party states, desiring by common action to improve their institutional facilities and provide
27 programs of sufficiently high quality for the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of various types of
28 offenders, declare that it is the policy of each of the party states to provide such facilities and programs on the
- 54 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 basis of cooperation with one another, thereby serving the best interests of such offenders and of society. The
2 purpose of this compact is to provide for the development and execution of such programs of cooperation for
3 the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of offenders.
4 ARTICLE II
5 DEFINITIONS
6 As used in this compact, unless the context clearly requires otherwise:
7 (1) "state" means a state of the United States or, subject to the limitation contained in Article VII,
8 Guam;
9 (2) "sending state" means a state party to this compact in which conviction was had;
10 (3) "receiving state" means a state party to this compact to which an inmate is sent for confinement
11 other than a state in which conviction was had;
12 (4) "inmate" means a male or female, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], offender who is under
13 sentence to or confined in a prison or other correctional institution;
14 (5) "institution" means any prison, reformatory, or other correctional facility (including but not
15 limited to a facility for the mentally ill or mentally defective) in which inmates may lawfully be confined.
16 ARTICLE III
17 CONTRACTS
18 (1) Each party state may make one or more contracts with any one or more of the other party
19 states for the confinement of inmates on behalf of a sending state in institutions situated within receiving states.
20 Any such contract shall provide for:
21 (a) its duration;
22 (b) payments to be made to the receiving state by the sending state for inmate maintenance,
23 extraordinary medical and dental expenses, and any participation in or receipt by inmates of rehabilitative or
24 correctional services, facilities, programs, or treatment not reasonably included as part of normal maintenance;
25 (c) participation in programs of inmate employment, if any; the disposition or crediting of any
26 payments received by inmates on account thereof; and the crediting of proceeds from or disposal of any
27 products resulting therefrom;
28 (d) delivery and retaking of inmates;
- 55 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (e) such other matters as may be necessary and appropriate to fix the obligations, responsibilities,
2 and rights of the sending and receiving states.
3 (2) Prior to the construction or completion of construction of any institution or addition thereto by a
4 party state, any other party state or states may contract therewith for the enlargement of the planned capacity
5 of the institution or addition thereto, or for the inclusion therein of particular equipment or structures, and for the
6 reservation of a specific percent of the capacity of the institution to be kept available for use by inmates of the
7 sending state or states so contracting. Any sending state so contracting may, to the extent that moneys are
8 legally available therefor, pay to the receiving state a reasonable sum as consideration for such enlargement of
9 capacity or provision of equipment or structures and reservation of capacity. Such payment may be in a lump
10 sum or in installments as provided in the contract.
11 (3) The terms and provisions of this compact shall be a part of any contract entered into by the
12 authority of or pursuant thereto, and nothing in any such contract shall be inconsistent therewith.
13 ARTICLE IV
14 PROCEDURES AND RIGHTS
15 (1) Whenever the duly constituted judicial or administrative authorities in a state party to this
16 compact, and which has entered into a contract pursuant to Article III, shall decide that confinement in or
17 transfer of an inmate to an institution within the territory of another party state is necessary in order to provide
18 adequate quarters and care or desirable in order to provide an appropriate program of rehabilitation or
19 treatment, said officials may direct that the confinement be within an institution within the territory of said other
20 party state, the receiving state to act in that regard solely as agent for the sending state.
21 (2) The appropriate officials of any state party to this compact shall have access at all reasonable
22 times to any institution in which it has a contractual right to confine inmates for the purpose of inspecting the
23 facilities thereof and visiting such of its inmates as may be confined in the institution.
24 (3) Inmates confined in an institution pursuant to the terms of this compact shall at all times be
25 subject to the jurisdiction of the sending state and may at any time be removed therefrom for transfer to a
26 prison or other institution within the sending state, for transfer to another institution in which the sending state
27 may have a contractual or other right to confine inmates, for release on probation or parole, for discharge, or for
28 any other purpose permitted by the laws of the sending state; provided that the sending state shall continue to
- 56 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 be obligated to such payments as may be required pursuant to the terms of any contract entered into under the
2 terms of Article III.
3 (4) Each receiving state shall provide regular reports to each sending state on the inmates of that
4 sending state in institutions pursuant to this compact including a conduct record of each inmate and certify said
5 record to the official designated by the sending state in order that each inmate may have the benefit of the
6 inmate's record in determining and altering the disposition of said inmate in accordance with the law which may
7 obtain in the sending state and in order that the same may be a source of information for the sending state.
8 (5) All inmates who may be confined in an institution pursuant to the provisions of this compact
9 shall be treated in a reasonable and humane manner and shall be cared for and treated equally with such
10 similar inmates of the receiving state as may be confined in the same institution. The fact of confinement in a
11 receiving state shall not deprive any inmate so confined of any legal rights which said inmate would have had if
12 confined in an appropriate institution of the sending state.
13 (6) Any hearing or hearings to which an inmate confined pursuant to this compact may be entitled
14 by the laws of the sending state may be had before the appropriate authorities of the sending state or of the
15 receiving state if authorized by the sending state. The receiving state shall provide adequate facilities for such
16 hearings as may be conducted by the appropriate officials of a sending state. In the event such hearing or
17 hearings are had before officials of the receiving state, the governing law shall be that of the sending state and
18 a record of the hearing or hearings as prescribed by the sending state shall be made. Said record together with
19 any recommendations of the hearing officials shall be transmitted forthwith to the official or officials before
20 whom the hearing would have been had if it had taken place in the sending state. In any and all proceedings
21 had pursuant to the provisions of this subdivision, the officials of the receiving state shall act solely as agents of
22 the sending state and no final determination shall be made in any matter except by the appropriate officials of
23 the sending state. Costs of records made pursuant to this subsection shall be borne by the sending state.
24 (7) Any inmate confined pursuant to this compact shall be released within the territory of the
25 sending state unless the inmate and the sending and receiving states shall agree upon release in some other
26 place. The sending state shall bear the cost of such return to its territory.
27 (8) Any inmate confined pursuant to the terms of this compact shall have any and all rights to
28 participate in and derive any benefits, incur or be relieved of any obligations, or have such obligations modified
- 57 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 or the inmate's status changed on account of any action or proceeding in which the inmate could have
2 participated if confined in any appropriate institution of the sending state located within such state.
3 (9) The parent, guardian, trustee, or other person or persons entitled under the laws of the sending
4 state to act for, advise, or otherwise function with respect to any inmate shall not be deprived of or restricted in
5 the person's exercise of any power in respect of any inmate confined pursuant to the terms of this compact.
6 ARTICLE V
7 ACTS NOT REVIEWABLE IN RECEIVING STATE -- EXTRADITION
8 (1) Any decision of the sending state in respect of any matter over which it retains jurisdiction
9 pursuant to this compact shall be conclusive upon and not reviewable within the receiving state, but if at the
10 time the sending state seeks to remove an inmate from an institution in the receiving state there is pending
11 against the inmate within such state any criminal charge or if the inmate is suspected of having committed
12 within such state a criminal offense, the inmate shall not be returned without the consent of the receiving state
13 until discharged from prosecution or other form of proceeding, imprisonment, or detention for such offense. The
14 duly accredited officers of the sending state shall be permitted to transport inmates pursuant to this compact
15 through any and all states party to this compact without interference.
16 (2) An inmate who escapes from an institution in which the inmate is confined pursuant to this
17 compact shall be deemed a fugitive from the sending state and from the state in which the institution is situated.
18 In the case of an escape to a jurisdiction other than the sending or receiving state, the responsibility for
19 institution of extradition proceedings shall be that of the sending state, but nothing contained herein shall be
20 construed to prevent or affect the activities of officers and agencies of any jurisdiction directed toward the
21 apprehension and return of an escapee.
22 ARTICLE VI
23 FEDERAL AID
24 Any state party to this compact may accept federal aid for use in connection with any institution or
25 program, the use of which is or may be affected by this compact or any contract pursuant hereto, and any
26 inmate in a receiving state pursuant to this compact may participate in any such federally aided program or
27 activity for which the sending and receiving states have made contractual provision, provided that, if such
28 program or activity is not part of the customary correctional regimen, the express consent of the appropriate
- 58 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 official of the sending state shall be required therefor.
2 ARTICLE VII
3 ENTRY INTO FORCE
4 This compact shall enter into force and become effective and binding upon the states so acting when it
5 has been enacted into law by any two contiguous states from among the states of Alaska, Arizona, California,
6 Colorado, Hawaii, Idaho, Montana, Nebraska, Nevada, New Mexico, Oregon, Utah, Washington, and Wyoming.
7 For the purposes of this article, Alaska and Hawaii shall be deemed contiguous to each other; to any and all of
8 the states of California, Oregon, and Washington; and to Guam. Thereafter, this compact shall enter into force
9 and become effective and binding as to any other of said states or any other state contiguous to at least one
10 party state upon similar action by such state. Guam may become party to this compact by taking action similar
11 to that provided for joinder by any other eligible party state and upon the consent of congress to such joinder.
12 For the purposes of this article, Guam shall be deemed contiguous to Alaska, Hawaii, California, Oregon, and
13 Washington.
14 ARTICLE VIII
15 WITHDRAWAL AND TERMINATION
16 This compact shall continue in force and remain binding upon a party state until it shall have enacted a
17 statute repealing the same and providing for the sending of formal written notice of withdrawal from the
18 compact to the appropriate officials of all other party states. An actual withdrawal shall not take effect until 2
19 years after the notices provided in said statute have been sent. Such withdrawal shall not relieve the
20 withdrawing state from its obligations assumed hereunder prior to the effective date of withdrawal. Before the
21 effective date of withdrawal, a withdrawing state shall remove to its territory, at its own expense, such inmates
22 as it may have confined pursuant to the provisions of this compact.
23 ARTICLE IX
24 OTHER ARRANGEMENTS UNAFFECTED
25 Nothing contained in this compact shall be construed to abrogate or impair any agreement or other
26 arrangement which a party state may have with a nonparty state for the confinement, rehabilitation, or
27 treatment of inmates or to repeal any other laws of a party state authorizing the making of cooperative
28 institutional arrangements.
- 59 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 ARTICLE X
2 CONSTRUCTION AND SEVERABILITY
3 The provisions of this compact shall be liberally construed and shall be severable. If any phrase,
4 clause, sentence, or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of any participating
5 state or of the United States or the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person, or circumstance is
6 held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact and the applicability thereof to any government,
7 agency, person, or circumstance shall not be affected thereby. If this compact shall be held contrary to the
8 constitution of any state participating therein, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the
9 remaining states and in full force and effect as to the state affected as to all severable matters."

11 Section 43. Section 46-19-401, MCA, is amended to read:

14 INTERSTATE CORRECTIONS COMPACT
15 ARTICLE I
16 PURPOSE AND POLICY
17 The party states, desiring by common action to fully utilize and improve their institutional facilities and
18 provide adequate programs for the confinement, treatment and rehabilitation of various types of offenders,
19 declare that it is the policy of each of the party states to provide such facilities and programs on a basis of
20 cooperation with one another, thereby serving the best interests of such offenders and of society and effecting
21 economies in capital expenditures and operational costs. The purpose of this compact is to provide for the
22 mutual development and execution of such programs of cooperation for the confinement, treatment and
23 rehabilitation of offenders with the most economical use of human and material resources.
24 ARTICLE II
25 DEFINITIONS

5 (d) "Inmate" means a male or female, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], offender who is committed
6 under sentence to or confined in a penal or correctional institution.

24 (b) The terms and provisions of this compact shall be a part of any contract entered into by the
25 authority of or pursuant thereto, and nothing in any such contract shall be inconsistent therewith.
26 ARTICLE IV
27 PROCEDURES AND RIGHTS
28 (a) Whenever the duly constituted authorities in a state party to this compact, and which has
- 61 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 entered into a contract pursuant to Article III, shall decide that confinement in, or transfer of an inmate to, an
2 institution within the territory of another party state is necessary or desirable in order to provide adequate
3 quarters and care or an appropriate program of rehabilitation or treatment, said officials may direct that the
4 confinement be within an institution within the territory of said other party state, the receiving state to act in that
5 regard solely as agent for the sending state.
6 (b) The appropriate officials of any state party to this compact shall have access, at all reasonable
7 times, to any institution in which it has a contractual right to confine inmates for the purpose of inspecting the
8 facilities thereof and visiting such of its inmates as may be confined in the institution.
9 (c) Inmates confined in an institution pursuant to the terms of this compact shall at all times be
10 subject to the jurisdiction of the sending state and may at any time be removed therefrom for transfer to a
11 prison or other institution within the sending state. For transfer to another institution in which the sending state
12 may have a contractual or other right to confine inmates, for release on probation or parole, for discharge, or for
13 any other purpose permitted by the laws of the sending state; provided that the sending state shall continue to
14 be obligated to such payments as may be required pursuant to the terms of any contract entered into under the
15 terms of Article III.
16 (d) Each receiving state shall provide regular reports to each sending state on the inmates of that
17 sending state in institutions pursuant to this compact including a conduct record of each inmate and certify said
18 record to the official designated by the sending state, in order that each inmate may have official review of the
19 inmate's record in determining and altering the disposition of said inmate in accordance with the law which may
20 obtain in the sending state and in order that the same may be a source of information for the sending state.
21 (e) All inmates who may be confined in an institution pursuant to the provisions of this compact
22 shall be treated in a reasonable and humane manner and shall be treated equally with such similar inmates of
23 the receiving state as may be confined in the same institution. The fact of confinement in a receiving state shall
24 not deprive any inmate so confined of any legal rights which said inmate would have had if confined in an
25 appropriate institution of the sending state.
26 (f) Any hearing or hearings to which an inmate confined pursuant to this compact may be entitled
27 by the laws of the sending state may be had before the appropriate authorities of the sending state, or of the
28 receiving state if authorized by the sending state. The receiving state shall provide adequate facilities for such
- 62 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 hearings as may be conducted by the appropriate officials of a sending state. In the event such hearing or
2 hearings are had before officials of the receiving state, the governing law shall be that of the sending state and
3 a record of the hearing or hearings as prescribed by the sending state shall be made. Said record together with
4 any recommendations of the hearing officials shall be transmitted forthwith to the official or officials before
5 whom the hearing would have been had if it had taken place in the sending state. In any and all proceedings
6 had pursuant to the provisions of this subsection, the officials of the receiving state shall act solely as agents of
7 the sending state and no final determination shall be made in any matter except by the appropriate officials of
8 the sending state.
9 (g) Any inmate confined pursuant to this compact shall be released within the territory of the
10 sending state unless the inmate, and the sending and receiving states, shall agree upon release in some other
11 place. The sending state shall bear the cost of such return to its territory.
12 (h) Any inmate confined pursuant to the terms of this compact shall have any and all rights to
13 participate in and derive any benefits or incur or be relieved of any obligations or have such obligations
14 modified or the inmate's status changed on account of any action or proceeding in which the inmate could have
15 participated if confined in any appropriate institution of the sending state located within such state.
16 (i) The parent, guardian, trustee, or other person or persons entitled under the laws of the sending
17 state to act for, advise, or otherwise function with respect to any inmate shall not be deprived of or restricted in
18 the inmate's exercise of any power in respect of any inmate confined pursuant to the terms of this compact.
19 ARTICLE V
20 ACTS NOT REVIEWABLE IN RECEIVING STATE -- EXTRADITION
21 (a) Any decision of the sending state in respect of any matter over which it retains jurisdiction
22 pursuant to this compact shall be conclusive upon and not reviewable within the receiving state, but if at the
23 time the sending state seeks to remove an inmate from an institution in the receiving state there is pending
24 against the inmate within such state any criminal charge or if the inmate is formally accused of having
25 committed within such state a criminal offense, the inmate shall not be returned without the consent of the
26 receiving state until discharged from prosecution or other form of proceeding, imprisonment or detention for
27 such offense. The duly accredited officers of the sending state shall be permitted to transport inmates pursuant
28 to this compact through any and all states party to this compact without interference.
- 63 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (b) An inmate who escapes from an institution in which the inmate is confined pursuant to this
2 compact shall be deemed a fugitive from the sending state and from the state in which the institution is situated.
3 In the case of an escape to a jurisdiction other than the sending or receiving state, the responsibility for
4 institution of extradition or rendition proceedings shall be that of the sending state, but nothing contained herein
5 shall be construed to prevent or affect the activities of officers and agencies of any jurisdiction directed toward
6 the apprehension and return of an escapee.
7 ARTICLE VI
8 FEDERAL AID
9 Any state party to this compact may accept federal aid for use in connection with any institution or
10 program, the use of which is or may be affected by this compact or any contract pursuant hereto and any
11 inmate in a receiving state pursuant to this compact may participate in any such federally aided program or
12 activity for which the sending and receiving states have made contractual provision, provided that if such
13 program or activity is not part of the customary correctional regimen, the express consent of the appropriate
14 official of the sending state shall be required therefor.
15 ARTICLE VII
16 ENTRY INTO FORCE
17 This compact shall enter into force and become effective and binding upon the states so acting when it
18 has been enacted into law by any two states. Thereafter, this compact shall enter into force and become
19 effective and binding as to any other of said states upon similar action by such state.
20 ARTICLE VIII
21 WITHDRAWAL AND TERMINATION
22 This compact shall continue in force and remain binding upon a party state until it shall have enacted a
23 statute repealing the same and providing for the sending of formal written notice of withdrawal from the
24 compact to the appropriate officials of all other party states. An actual withdrawal shall not take effect until one
25 year after the notices provided in said statute have been sent. Such withdrawal shall not relieve the withdrawing
26 state from its obligations assumed hereunder prior to the effective date of withdrawal. Before the effective date
27 of withdrawal, a withdrawing state shall remove to its territory, at its own expense, such inmates as it may have
28 confined pursuant to the provisions of this compact.
- 64 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 ARTICLE IX
2 OTHER ARRANGEMENTS UNAFFECTED
3 Nothing contained in this compact shall be construed to abrogate or impair any agreement or other
4 arrangement which a party state may have with a nonparty state for the confinement, rehabilitation or treatment
5 of inmates nor to repeal any other laws of a party state authorizing the making of cooperative institutional
6 arrangements.
7 ARTICLE X
8 CONSTRUCTION AND SEVERABILITY
9 The provisions of this compact shall be liberally construed and shall be severable. If any phrase,
10 clause, sentence or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of any participating
11 state or of the United States or the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person or circumstance is
12 held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact and the applicability thereof to any government,
13 agency, person or circumstance shall not be affected thereby. If this compact shall be held contrary to the
14 constitution of any state participating therein, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the
15 remaining states and in full force and effect as to the state affected as to all severable matters."
16
17 Section 44. Section 49-1-102, MCA, is amended to read:
18 "49-1-102. Freedom from discrimination. (1) The right to be free from discrimination because of
19 race, creed, religion, color, sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], physical or mental disability, age, or national
20 origin is recognized as and declared to be a civil right. This right must include but not be limited to:

23 of public resort, accommodation, assemblage, or amusement.

25 relevant information concerning the factors listed in subsection (1). Consideration of religious factors by a
26 licensed child-placing agency that is affiliated with a particular religious faith is not arbitrary consideration of
27 religion within the meaning of this section."

28 the path of travel to the altered primary function area and the restrooms, telephones, and drinking fountains
- 75 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 serving the altered primary function area are readily accessible and usable by persons with disabilities.
2 (2) (a) A person or entity is not required to make alterations to provide an accessible path of travel
3 to an altered primary function area if in terms of cost and scope the alterations to the path of travel are
4 disproportionate to the cost of the alterations to the primary function area. Alterations to a path of travel to an
5 altered primary function area must be considered disproportionate if the cost exceeds 20% of the cost of the
6 alterations to the primary function area. This subsection does not prohibit an expenditure to alter a path of travel
7 that exceeds 20% of the cost of the alterations to a primary function area.
8 (b) If the cost of altering a path of travel to an altered primary function area is disproportionate as
9 provided in subsection (2)(a), the path of travel must be made accessible to the extent possible without
10 incurring disproportionate costs. The alterations to the path of travel must be made by providing, in the following
11 order or priority:
12 (i) an accessible entrance and accessible exterior route to the accessible entrance from
13 accessible parking and passenger loading zones or from a public sidewalk if the public sidewalk is immediately
14 adjacent to the public building site;
15 (ii) an accessible path of travel to the altered primary function area;
16 (iii) accessible restrooms for each sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], or a single unisex
17 restroom when allowed by the applicable building code; and
18 (iv) accessible elements, including but not limited to storage spaces and alarms.
19 (3) A person or entity subject to the provisions of this section is also subject to the provisions of 50-
20 60-213(5)(a) and (5)(b)."

14 Section 57. Section 53-21-142, MCA, is amended to read:
15 "53-21-142. Rights of persons admitted to facility. Patients admitted to a mental health facility,
16 whether voluntarily or involuntarily, have the following rights:
17 (1) Patients have a right to privacy and dignity.
18 (2) Patients have a right to the least restrictive conditions necessary to achieve the purposes of
19 commitment. Patients must be accorded the right to appropriate treatment and related services in a setting and
20 under conditions that:
21 (a) are the most supportive of the patient's personal liberty; and
22 (b) restrict the patient's liberty only to the extent necessary and consistent with the patient's
23 treatment need, applicable requirements of law, and judicial orders.
24 (3) Patients have rights to visitation and reasonable access to telephone communications,
25 including the right to converse with others privately, except to the extent that the professional person
26 responsible for formulation of a particular patient's treatment plan writes an order imposing special restrictions.
27 The written order must be renewed after each periodic review of the treatment plan if any restrictions are to be
28 continued. Patients have an unrestricted right to visitation with attorneys, with spiritual counselors, and with
- 80 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 private physicians and other professional persons.

3 receive sealed mail from their attorneys, private physicians and other professional persons, the mental
4 disabilities board of visitors, courts, and government officials. Patients have a right to receive sealed mail from
5 others except to the extent that a professional person responsible for formulation of a particular patient's
6 treatment plan writes an order imposing special restrictions on receipt of sealed mail. The written order must be
7 renewed after each periodic review of the treatment plan if any restrictions are to be continued.
8 (5) Patients have an unrestricted right to have access to letter-writing materials, including postage,
9 and have a right to have staff members of the facility assist persons who are unable to write, prepare, and mail
10 correspondence.
11 (6) Patients have a right to wear their own clothes and to keep and use their own personal
12 possessions, including toilet articles, except to the extent that clothes or personal possessions may be
13 determined by a professional person in charge of the patient's treatment plan to be dangerous or otherwise
14 inappropriate to the treatment regimen. The facility has an obligation to supply an adequate allowance of
15 clothing to any patients who do not have suitable clothing of their own. Patients must have the opportunity to
16 select from various types of neat, clean, and seasonable clothing. The clothing must be considered the patient's
17 throughout the patient's stay at the facility. The facility shall make provision for the laundering of patient
18 clothing.
19 (7) Patients have the right to keep and be allowed to spend a reasonable sum of their own money.
20 (8) Patients have the right to religious worship. Provisions for worship must be made available to
21 all patients on a nondiscriminatory basis. An individual may not be required to engage in any religious activities.
22 (9) Patients have a right to regular physical exercise several times a week. The facility shall
23 provide facilities and equipment for physical exercise. Patients have a right to be outdoors at regular and
24 frequent intervals in the absence of contrary medical considerations.
25 (10) Patients have the right to be provided, with adequate supervision, suitable opportunities for
26 interaction with members of the opposite sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], except to the extent that a
27 professional person in charge of the patient's treatment plan writes an order stating that the interaction is

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (11) Patients have a right to receive prompt and adequate medical treatment for any physical
2 ailments. In providing medical care, the mental health facility shall take advantage of whatever community-
3 based facilities are appropriate and available and shall coordinate the patient's treatment for mental illness with
4 the patient's medical treatment.
5 (12) Patients have a right to a diet that will provide at a minimum the recommended daily dietary
6 allowances as developed by the national academy of sciences. Provisions must be made for special
7 therapeutic diets and for substitutes at the request of the patient or the friend of respondent in accordance with
8 the religious requirements of any patient's faith. Denial of a nutritionally adequate diet may not be used as
9 punishment.
10 (13) Patients have a right to a humane psychological and physical environment within the mental
11 health facilities. These facilities must be designed to afford patients with comfort and safety, promote dignity,
12 and ensure privacy. The facilities must be designed to make a positive contribution to the efficient attainment of
13 the treatment goals set for the patient. In order to ensure the accomplishment of this goal:
14 (a) regular housekeeping and maintenance procedures that will ensure that the facility is
15 maintained in a safe, clean, and attractive condition must be developed and implemented;
16 (b) there must be special provision made for geriatric and other nonambulatory patients to ensure
17 their safety and comfort, including special fittings on toilets and wheelchairs. Appropriate provision must be
18 made to permit nonambulatory patients to communicate their needs to the facility staff.
19 (c) pursuant to an established routine maintenance and repair program, the physical plant of each
20 facility must be kept in a continuous state of good repair and operation in accordance with the needs of the
21 health, comfort, safety, and well-being of the patients;
22 (d) each facility must meet all fire and safety standards established by the state and locality. In
23 addition, any hospital must meet the provisions of the life safety code of the national fire protection association
24 that are applicable to hospitals. A hospital must meet all standards established by the state for general
25 hospitals to the extent that they are relevant to psychiatric facilities.

27 (a) to be informed of the rights described in this section at the time of admission and periodically
28 after admission in language and terms appropriate to the patient's condition and ability to understand;
- 82 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (b) to assert grievances with respect to infringement of the rights described in this section,
2 including the right to have a grievance considered in a fair and timely manner according to an impartial
3 grievance procedure that must be provided for by the facility; and
4 (c) to exercise the rights described in this section without reprisal and may not be denied
5 admission to the facility as reprisal for the exercise of the rights described in this section.
6 (15) In order to assist a person admitted to a program or facility in the exercise or protection of the
7 patient's rights, the patient's attorney, advocate, or legal representatives must be given reasonable access to:
8 (a) the patient;
9 (b) the program or facility areas where the patient has received treatment or has resided or the
10 areas to which the patient has had access; and
11 (c) pursuant to the written authorization of the patient, records and information pertaining to the
12 patient's diagnosis, treatment, and related services.
13 (16) A person admitted to a facility must be given access to any available individual or service that
14 provides advocacy for the protection of the person's rights and that assists the person in understanding,
15 exercising, and protecting the person's rights as described in this section.
16 (17) This section may not:
17 (a) obligate a professional person to administer treatment contrary to the professional's clinical
18 judgment;
19 (b) prevent a facility from discharging a patient for whom appropriate treatment, consistent with the
20 clinical judgment of a professional person responsible for the patient's treatment, is or has become impossible
21 to administer because of the patient's refusal to consent to the treatment;
22 (c) require a facility to admit a person who has, on prior occasions, repeatedly withheld consent to
23 appropriate treatment; or
24 (d) obligate a facility to treat a person admitted to the facility solely for diagnostic evaluation."

10 SECTION 59. Section 53-30-312, MCA, is amended to read:
11 "53-30-312. Creation of community corrections boards -- membership -- appointment -- terms --
12 compensation. (1) A unit of local government, the governing bodies of two or more units of local government,
13 or a tribal government may establish a community corrections board.
14 (2) A community corrections board consists of three to seven members, must, when possible, be
15 gender-balanced, as provided in [section 1], and have racial parity, and must include:
16 (a) one local law enforcement officer;
17 (b) one probation and parole officer; and
18 (c) one member of the public.
19 (3) Members of a community corrections board must be appointed by the chief executive officer of
20 the unit of local government or the tribal government in the judicial district in which community corrections
21 facilities or programs are established.
22 (4) Members of a community corrections board shall serve for a term of 4 years.
23 (5) Members of a community corrections board shall serve without compensation except as
24 otherwise decided by the units of local government or a tribal government."

2 (b) any other nonprobate transfer at death.
3 (5) "Child" includes an individual entitled to take as a child under chapters 1 through 5 by intestate
4 succession from the parent whose relationship is involved and excludes a person who is only a stepchild, a
5 foster child, a grandchild, or any more remote descendant.
6 (6) (a) "Claims", in respect to estates of decedents and protected persons, includes liabilities of the
7 decedent or protected person, whether arising in contract, in tort, or otherwise, and liabilities of the estate that
8 arise at or after the death of the decedent or after the appointment of a conservator, including funeral expenses
9 and expenses of administration.
10 (b) The term does not include estate taxes or demands or disputes regarding title of a decedent or
11 protected person to specific assets alleged to be included in the estate.
12 (7) "Clerk" or "clerk of court" means the clerk of the district court.
13 (8) "Conservator" means a person who is appointed by a court to manage the estate of a protected
14 person.
15 (9) "Court" means the district court in this state having jurisdiction in matters relating to the affairs
16 of decedents.
17 (10) "Descendant" of an individual means all of the individual's descendants of all generations, with
18 the relationship of parent and child at each generation being determined by the definition of child and parent
19 contained in this code.
20 (11) "Devise" when used as a noun means a testamentary disposition of real or personal property
21 and when used as a verb means to dispose of real or personal property by will.
22 (12) "Devisee" means a person designated in a will to receive a devise. For purposes of chapter 3,
23 in the case of a devise to an existing trust or trustee or to a trustee or trust described by will, the trust or trustee
24 is the devisee and the beneficiaries are not devisees.
25 (13) "Disability" means cause for a protective order as described by 72-5-409.
26 (14) "Distributee" means any person who has received property of a decedent from the decedent's
27 personal representative other than as a creditor or purchaser. A testamentary trustee is a distributee only to the
28 extent of distributed assets or increment to distributed assets remaining in the trustee's hands. A beneficiary of
- 90 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 a testamentary trust to whom the trustee has distributed property received from a personal representative is a
2 distributee of the personal representative. For purposes of this provision, "testamentary trustee" includes a
3 trustee to whom assets are transferred by will, to the extent of the devised assets.
4 (15) "Estate" includes the property of the decedent, trust, or other person whose affairs are subject
5 to chapters 1 through 5 as originally constituted and as it exists from time to time during administration.
6 (16) "Exempt property" means that property of a decedent's estate that is described in 72-2-413.
7 (17) "Fiduciary" includes a personal representative, guardian, conservator, and trustee.
8 (18) "Foreign personal representative" means a personal representative appointed by another
9 jurisdiction.
10 (19) "Formal proceedings" means proceedings conducted before a judge with notice to interested
11 persons.
12 (20) "Governing instrument" means a deed; will; trust; insurance or annuity policy; account with
13 POD designation; security registered in beneficiary form (TOD); pension, profit-sharing, retirement, or similar
14 benefit plan; instrument creating or exercising a power of appointment or a power of attorney; or dispositive,
15 appointive, or nominative instrument of any similar type.
16 (21) "Guardian" means a person who has qualified as a guardian of a minor or incapacitated person
17 pursuant to testamentary or court appointment but excludes one who is merely a guardian ad litem.
18 (22) "Heirs", except as controlled by 72-2-721, means persons, including the surviving spouse and
19 the state, who are entitled under the statutes of intestate succession to the property of a decedent.
20 (23) "Incapacitated person" has the meaning provided in 72-5-101.
21 (24) "Informal proceedings" means proceedings conducted without notice to interested persons by
22 the clerk of court for probate of a will or appointment of a personal representative.
23 (25) "Interested person" includes heirs, devisees, children, spouses, creditors, beneficiaries, and
24 any others having a property right in or claim against a trust estate or the estate of a decedent, ward, or
25 protected person. The term also includes persons having priority for appointment as personal representative
26 and other fiduciaries representing interested persons. The meaning as it relates to particular persons may vary
27 from time to time and must be determined according to the particular purposes of and matter involved in any
28 proceeding.
- 91 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (26) "Issue" of a person means a descendant.
2 (27) "Joint tenants with the right of survivorship" includes co-owners of property held under
3 circumstances that entitle one or more to the whole of the property on the death of the other or others but
4 excludes forms of co-ownership registration in which the underlying ownership of each party is in proportion to
5 that party's contribution.
6 (28) "Lease" includes an oil, gas, coal, or other mineral lease.
7 (29) "Letters" includes letters testamentary, letters of guardianship, letters of administration, and
8 letters of conservatorship.
9 (30) "Minor" means a person who is under 18 years of age.
10 (31) "Mortgage" means any conveyance, agreement, or arrangement in which property is used as
11 security.
12 (32) "Nonresident decedent" means a decedent who was domiciled in another jurisdiction at the
13 time of death.
14 (33) "Organization" means a corporation, business trust, estate, trust, partnership, joint venture,
15 association, government or governmental subdivision or agency, or any other legal or commercial entity.
16 (34) "Parent" includes any person entitled to take, or who would be entitled to take if the child died
17 without a will, as a parent under chapters 1 through 5 by intestate succession from the child whose relationship
18 is in question and excludes any person who is only a stepparent, foster parent, or grandparent.
19 (35) "Payor" means a trustee, insurer, business entity, employer, government, governmental agency
20 or subdivision, or any other person authorized or obligated by law or a governing instrument to make payments.
21 (36) "Person" means an individual, a corporation, an organization, or other legal entity.
22 (37) "Personal representative" includes executor, administrator, successor personal representative,
23 special administrator, and persons who perform substantially the same function under the law governing their
24 status. "General personal representative" excludes special administrator.
25 (38) "Petition" means a written request to the court for an order after notice.
26 (39) "Proceeding" includes action at law and suit in equity.
27 (40) "Property" includes both real and personal property or any interest in that property and means
28 anything that may be the subject of ownership.
- 92 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (41) "Protected person" has the meaning provided in 72-5-101.
2 (42) "Protective proceeding" has the meaning provided in 72-5-101.
3 (43) "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an
4 electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
5 (44) "Security" includes any note; stock; treasury stock; bond; debenture; evidence of indebtedness;
6 certificate of interest or participation in an oil, gas, or mining title or lease or in payments out of production
7 under such a title or lease; collateral trust certificate; transferable share; voting trust certificate; in general, any
8 interest or instrument commonly known as a security; any certificate of interest or participation; or any
9 temporary or interim certificate, receipt, or certificate of deposit for or any warrant or right to subscribe to or
10 purchase any of the foregoing.
11 (45) "Settlement", in reference to a decedent's estate, includes the full process of administration,
12 distribution, and closing.
13 (46) "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record other than a will:
14 (a) to execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
15 (b) to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic symbol, sound, or process.
16 (47) "Special administrator" means a personal representative as described by chapter 3, part 7.
17 (48) "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, the Commonwealth of
18 Puerto Rico, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
19 (49) "Successor personal representative" means a personal representative, other than a special
20 administrator, who is appointed to succeed a previously appointed personal representative.
21 (50) "Successors" means persons, other than creditors, who are entitled to property of a decedent
22 under the decedent's will or chapters 1 through 5.
23 (51) "Supervised administration" refers to the proceedings described in chapter 3, part 4.
24 (52) "Survive" means that an individual has neither predeceased an event, including the death of
25 another individual, nor is considered to have predeceased an event under 72-2-114 or 72-2-712. The term
26 includes its derivatives, such as "survives", "survived", "survivor", and "surviving".
27 (53) "Testacy proceeding" means a proceeding to establish a will or determine intestacy.
28 (54) "Testator" includes an individual of either sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1].

1 (55) "Trust" includes an express trust, private or charitable, with additions to the trust, wherever and
2 however created. The term also includes a trust created or determined by judgment or decree under which the
3 trust is to be administered in the manner of an express trust. The term excludes other constructive trusts and
4 excludes resulting trusts; conservatorships; personal representatives; trust accounts as defined in 72-6-111 and
5 Title 72, chapter 6, parts 2 and 3; custodial arrangements pursuant to chapter 26; business trusts providing for

10 confirmed by court.

13 (58) "Ward" means an individual described in 72-5-101.

15 revokes or revises another will, nominates a guardian, or expressly excludes or limits the right of an individual
16 or class to succeed to property of the decedent passing by intestate succession."

18 SECTION 64. Section 72-17-106, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "72-17-106. Statewide organ and tissue donation registry. (1) The department of justice shall
20 electronically transfer to the federally designated organ procurement organization all information that appears
21 on the front of a driver's license, including the name, gender, as provided in [section 1], date of birth, and most
22 recent address of any person who obtains a driver's license and who volunteers to donate organs or tissue
23 upon death, as provided in 61-5-301. The department of justice may charge actual costs for the first transfer of
24 information, as provided in subsection (5). However, all subsequent electronic transfers of donor information
25 must be at no charge to the federally designated organ procurement organization.
26 (2) Information obtained by the federally designated organ procurement organization must be used
27 for the purpose of establishing a statewide organ and tissue donation registry accessible to in-state, recognized
28 cadaveric organ and cadaveric tissue agencies for the recovery or placement of organs and tissue and to
- 94 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 procurement agencies in another state when a Montana resident is a donor of an anatomical gift and is not
2 located in the state at the time of death or immediately before the death of the donor.
3 (3) An organ or tissue donation organization may not obtain information from the organ and tissue
4 donation registry for the purpose of fundraising. Organ and tissue donation registry information may not be
5 further disseminated unless authorized in this section or by federal law. Dissemination of organ and tissue
6 donation registry information may be made by the organ procurement organization to a recognized, in-state
7 procurement agency for other tissue recovery or to an out-of-state, federally designated organ procurement
8 organization.
9 (4) The federally designated organ procurement organization may acquire donor information from
10 sources other than the department of justice.
11 (5) All reasonable costs associated with the creation and maintenance of the organ and tissue
12 donation registry, as determined by the department of justice, must be paid by the organ and tissue
13 procurement organizations. Any money collected by the department of justice must be deposited in an account
14 in the state special revenue fund established by the department of justice for the purpose of the payment of
15 reasonable costs associated with the development and maintenance of the organ and tissue donation registry
16 and necessary for the initial installation and setup for electronic transfer of the donor information.
17 (6) An individual does not need to participate in the organ and tissue donation registry to be a
18 donor of organs or tissue. The registry is intended to facilitate organ and tissue donation and not inhibit persons
19 from being donors upon death."
20
21 SECTION 65. Section 90-14-104, MCA, is amended to read:
22 "90-14-104. Commission on community service. (1) The governor shall appoint a commission on
23 community service composed of up to 15 members.
24 (2) Members must include a representative from a tribal government and from at least four state
25 agencies in the following functional areas:
26 (a) natural resources;
27 (b) human services;
28 (c) labor;
- 95 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 SB0437.2
1 (d) K-12 education;
2 (e) higher education; and
3 (f) military affairs.
4 (3) Members may include representatives from local government, not-for-profit agencies, federal
5 agencies, business, labor unions, volunteer groups, and private citizens.
6 (4) To the extent possible, membership of the commission must be balanced according to race,
7 ethnicity, age, gender, as provided in [section 1], and disabilities.
8 (5) The commission shall assist in the development and coordination of state community service
9 programs, integration of services, dissemination of information, recruitment of volunteers, recruitment and
10 training of volunteer crewleaders, development of materials, and evaluation of and accountability for the
11 services provided.
12 (6) Commission members are entitled to payment and reimbursement as provided in 2-15-122(5)."

14 NEW SECTION. Section 66. Repealer. The following section of the Montana Code Annotated is
15 repealed:
16 1-1-201. Terms of wide applicability.
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 67. Codification instruction. [Section 1] is intended to be codified as an
19 integral part of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, and the provisions of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, apply to [section 1].
20
21 NEW SECTION. Section 68. Severability. If a part of [this act] is invalid, all valid parts that are
22 severable from the invalid part remain in effect. If a part of [this act] is invalid in one or more of its applications,
23 the part remains in effect in all valid applications that are severable from the invalid applications.
24
25 NEW SECTION. Section 69. Effective date. [This act] is effective on passage and approval.
